Held in the Capital 51

May Fourth Movement Commemoration Meeting

The Nanjing Special City Party Department held a commemoration meeting in the main hall at 10:00 am on the 11th anniversary of the May Fourth Movement. About 200 representatives from various government ministries, departments, and mass organizations attended. Chairman Yang Xiji of the City Executive Committee reported after the ceremonial rites that during the 7th and 8th years of the Republic, Chinese politics were corrupt, foreign powers were forcing concessions, and the people's livelihood was declining to the extreme. At that time, it was the end of the European War, and the Paris Peace Conference opened. The European and American powers were preparing to shift their strength to continue to invade our country. Japanese imperialism seized the opportunity to take the lead, colluding with Cao Rulin, Zhang Zongchang, Lu Zongyu and others to rob our country of its sovereignty. Duan Qirui then followed Yuan Shikai in making a second tacit acknowledgement of the conditions for national subjugation, and continued to carry out huge loans, hoping to obtain the assistance of Japanese imperialism to consolidate his position. At that time, the lifeline of the country was hanging by a thread. The general students full of blood and courage, especially the students in Beiping who were directly under the control of the warlord government and the imperialist embassy, ​​were filled with grief and indignation in the autumn of life and death, and could not bear it any longer. They resolutely raised their arms and stood up to be the vanguard of the people. On May 4, 1919, they held a grand protest demonstration, violently beat the traitors, besieged the residences of the traitors, and attacked the warlord government and resisted imperialism. It shocked the whole country for a while. Students and businessmen in various places responded one after another, and evolved into a universal and great patriotic movement. The national spirit was promoted, the traitors converged, and the initiative of the modern national self-awareness and self-salvation movement in our country was launched. In terms of cultural movement, it was the first manifestation of ideological revolution; in terms of social movement, it was the beginning of people's participation in politics; in terms of diplomacy, it was the first step towards people's diplomacy; in terms of national liberation, it was the first page of the brilliant light of national revolution. For the youth students themselves, it was a new era of patriotic movement, and it was worth permanent commemoration. The great significance of holding this commemoration this year is: (1) From now on, thoughts and actions must be based on the Three Principles of the People; (2) To cultivate a sound revolutionary psychology; (3) To cultivate constructive knowledge and ability; (4) To devote ourselves to the revolution under the leadership of our Party; (5) To assist the central government in eradicating the remnants of warlords, and more importantly, the imperialist aggression of China. In addition to political and economic ways, cultural aggression is the most serious. Taking unequal treaties as amulets, Christian youth associations and other church schools are set up everywhere, filling the minds of young people with imperialist seeds and deeply dyeing feudal ideas. Good young people are anesthetized for a long time and easily become slaves of imperialism. Therefore, it is necessary to reclaim the right to education and resist imperialist cultural aggression in order to complete the unfinished achievements of the May Fourth Movement. Then Lai Lian, member of the City Executive Committee, delivered a poignant speech, and then shouted slogans and dispersed.

Jinan on the May Third Memorial Day 52

The whole city flies flags at half-mast to express condolences

All circles held a memorial meeting

Jinan Correspondence, the Jinan May Third Massacre is an unprecedented shame for the Chinese nation, and also the most tragic tragedy in the world. Therefore, the whole country is indignant and the gods are saddened. Time flies, and two years have passed. Although Jinan has been taken over, the terms of investigation and compensation have not yet been fulfilled by the Japanese side, causing thousands of compatriots who were killed to sink to the bottom of the sea, unable to rest in peace. On the occasion of the second anniversary of this tragic case, all parts of the country unanimously hold solemn and fierce commemorations to express their unforgettable memory, and the 400,000 people in Jinan have suffered the remaining fire of the Japanese massacre, and their personal pain is even more indignant. In the past few days, they have actively prepared for the memorial meeting. Today (3rd), all circles in the city will fly flags at half-mast and stop entertainment to express their condolences. All schools and factories will be closed for one day. All newspapers will publish supplements with various photos of the Japanese soldiers' massacre of Chinese people on May 3, 1928, to arouse public attention. Various groups and organizations also printed leaflets separately and distributed them along the streets. The people were extremely excited. The military authorities were deeply afraid that some villains would take the opportunity to disturb public order, so the garrison command and the public security bureau dispatched a large number of soldiers and police to strengthen their posts and guard the streets to avoid accidents. The Japanese Consul in Jinan, Nishida, knew that he was unreasonable. In addition to requesting the military and police to protect the Japanese expatriates, he also notified the Japanese in Jinan that they were not allowed to go out to avoid misunderstandings. Some Japanese even went to Qingdao to avoid it. The memorial meeting held by all circles was held in the Nan Guan Yan Wu Hall. From 8:00 am, staff from various agencies, people from all walks of life, and students from various schools went to the meeting in a column. More than 500 groups and about 100,000 people came to the meeting. Each held a small flag with various slogans and slogans written on it, and many people distributed leaflets on the spot. The atmosphere was extremely tense. A high platform was built on the north side of the Yan Wu Hall, with Party and national flags intertwined, a portrait of the Premier hanging, and the spirit tablets of the May Third martyrs erected as a place for the meeting and paying respects. A high pavilion was built on the south side as a place for the chief commander to issue orders. The staff of the conference were all assigned in advance. The chairman was He Siyuan, the propaganda minister of the Provincial Rectification Committee, the chief commander was Zhang Yixian, the director of the public sports field, the master of ceremonies was Yu Hongchan of the Municipal Rectification Committee, and the record was Wang Yumin of the Provincial Rectification Committee. The meeting started at 9:00 am. First, everyone stood in silence, played mourning music, and sang the Party song. Then, they bowed three times to the Party and national flags, the Premier's portrait, and the martyred compatriots. Then, Chairman He Siyuan respectfully read the Premier's will, and Ms. Gong Jixiang and Chen Zuzhen offered wreaths. Zheng Henian of the Municipal Rectification Committee read the memorial text, which said, "On May 3, 19th year of the Republic of China, the citizens of Jinan respectfully pay their respects to the spirits of the martyrs who were killed in the Jinan May Third Massacre and tell them in writing, alas, martyrs, born to be heroes, died to be spirits, suffered the red sheep catastrophe, sacrificed their lives to become benevolent, tracing the source of the disaster, starting from the violent Japan, doing whatever it wants, and getting an inch. The national revolution is for self-preservation, exterminating the power, and saving our people. Touching its jealousy, sending troops to Jiaoji, provoking incidents for no reason, and the disaster began. Killing our officials, slaughtering our people, blood flowing into rivers, corpses piling up like hills, burning our city, destroying our city walls, not enough, and even more looting for a year, always being ferocious, the living suffer pain, the dead are not at peace, after such a strange revenge, two years have passed, and it has not been avenged, and blood and tears are shed in vain, the martyrs have spirits, protect and inspire the dead, and do everything to eliminate Wu, to avenge this shame, alas, I respectfully inform you," after reading, Chairman He Siyuan reported the purpose of the meeting, briefly saying that on this day two years ago, Japanese soldiers opened fire on our Chinese compatriots in Jinan, massacring them. At 10:00 am, in the business district, Japanese soldiers fired at Chinese soldiers. Before the Chinese soldiers returned fire, they abducted more than 1,000 Chinese soldiers and brutally killed our country's diplomatic envoy, Cai Gongshi. On the 4th, they issued the Demands to our country, making various unreasonable demands, limiting the Chinese army to withdraw 20 li outside within seven hours, and implementing great insulting measures against the Chinese nation. China received demands from various countries, but none were as severe as those of the Japanese. Because China did not agree to its demands, Japan began to bomb the city with artillery on the 8th, killing more than 3,000 Chinese people and causing property losses of more than 50 million. I would like to ask, no matter which country, which people can do this kind of thing, only Japan dares to open fire in China and arbitrarily kill people. This is really a great shame for China. I hope that the Chinese people, especially the youth of Shandong, will never forget it until death, and must work hard to avenge this shame. Do you all know if Jinan has been resolved now? It hasn't been resolved at all. It has been more than a year since Jinan was taken over. The terms of sending people to investigate the Jinan case and compensate for losses have not yet been fulfilled by Japan. The Chinese investigators have already been sent, but Japan has been delaying and not sending them. Therefore, today's meeting has a proposal, which is to ask the central government to urge Japan to send investigators for the Jinan case as soon as possible in order to resolve the case as soon as possible. China has always compensated or ceded land for killing a foreigner. Last year, Japan killed a Chinese rickshaw puller in Qingdao, and only agreed to compensate 200 yuan. It really doesn't treat the Chinese people as human beings. You all have to think about whether we Shandong people are human beings or not. It can kill thousands of people and be done with it? We Chinese people are not for sale, we are demanding justice, fairness and humanity. The status of the Chinese nation, the imperialists of all countries, do not treat the Chinese people as human beings, we should concentrate our strength and overthrow all imperialism. After today's meeting, we must not forget the May Third Massacre at all times, do not forget the evil of Japan and all imperialists, unite and do everything to deal with him, etc. Then Zhang Jinjian, representative of the Provincial Rectification Committee, Zhang Hongjian of the Municipal Rectification Committee, Guo Yumin, representative of the United Association of Victims of the Jinan Case, Sun Ziyi, a student from the attached elementary school of the First Women's Normal School, Feng Xianzhou, a student from the senior high school, Hua Degang, a student from Yuying Middle School, Wang Ruyu, a student from Jimei Middle School, Qiu Zuming, a student from the Municipal Fifth Elementary School, Jiang Shifen, a student from the Fifth Experimental Elementary School, Rao Shuzhen, a student from the Municipal Third Elementary School, and Ms. Rao Shuzhen, gave speeches one after another, all of which were extremely passionate and慷慨. Finally, Song Zhixian of the Provincial Rectification Committee reported the proposals of the conference: (1) To telegraph the central government to transfer the national government to strictly implement revolutionary diplomacy; (2) To telegraph the central government to transfer the national government to order the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to urge the Japanese side to send investigators for the Jinan case as soon as possible in order to resolve the case as soon as possible; (3) To send a telegram to the whole country to jointly condemn Yan Xishan and Feng Yuxiang, who colluded with Japanese imperialism, to the public for deliberation, and all were approved. Then they shouted slogans and played music to dismiss the meeting. (May 3)

External Announcement 53

Full Text of the Sino-British Handover of Weihaiwei Case

The Ministry of Foreign Affairs today announced three documents regarding the Sino-British handover of Weihaiwei case: (1) The Sino-British Convention on the Recovery of Weihaiwei and its appendices; (2) Agreement and appendices; (3) The full text of the handover of Weihaiwei case is recorded as follows:

Special Agreement for the Handover of Weihaiwei between China and Britain 54

The Chairman of the National Government of the Republic of China and His Britannic Majesty, King of Great Britain and Ireland and of the British Dominions beyond the Seas, Emperor of India, desiring to effect the complete retrocession to China of the territory of Weihaiwei leased by China to Great Britain under the Convention of July 1, 1898, have resolved to conclude a Special Convention for the Rendition of Weihaiwei, and have appointed for this purpose as their Plenipotentiaries:

The Chairman of the National Government of the Republic of China, Wang Cheng-ting, Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Republic of China;

His Britannic Majesty, King of Great Britain and Ireland and of the British Dominions beyond the Seas, Emperor of India, for Great Britain and Northern Ireland, Sir Miles Lampson, His Britannic Majesty’s Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary to China;

Who, having communicated their full powers, found in good and due form, have agreed upon the following Articles:

Article 1. His Britannic Majesty cedes to the Republic of China the territory of Weihaiwei, comprising all the area within the boundary pillars erected by the Boundary Commission of 1899–1901, that is to say, the city of Weihaiwei, the ten-mile zone along the entire coastline of Weihaiwei Bay, and the island of Liu Kung Tao, and all other islands in Weihaiwei Bay.

Article 2. The Convention for the Lease of Weihaiwei of July 1, 1898, is hereby abrogated.

Article 3. All British armed forces stationed at Weihaiwei and Liu Kung Tao shall be completely withdrawn within one month from the date of the coming into force of this Convention.

Article 4. The British Government undertakes to hand over to the National Government of the Republic of China all archives, registers, title deeds, and other documents of the British Weihaiwei Administration which are relevant to the rendition and future administration of Weihaiwei by the Chinese Government.

Article 5. The British Government agrees to present to the National Government of the Republic of China all British Government property, land and buildings within the Weihaiwei area.

Article 6. The British Government agrees to hand over gratuitously to the National Government of the Republic of China all works undertaken and articles purchased in connection with the scheme for the improvement of the De Sheng Pier and the dockyard, including the launch "Galia."

Article 7. The British Government agrees to transfer gratuitously to the National Government of the Republic of China the telegraph line between Chefoo and Weihaiwei, and all public property in store, including the items specified in Annex 1.

Article 8. The British Government agrees to transfer gratuitously to the National Government of the Republic of China the civil hospitals at Edward Port and Hot Springs, including land, buildings, and equipment.

Article 9. The British Government agrees to return to the Chinese Government all original Chinese Government property, land and buildings on Liu Kung Tao, as well as land acquired by the British Government after the lease, and to hand over to the National Government of the Republic of China all leases of land and property rights to buildings on leased land that will revert to government ownership upon expiration of the leases.

Article 10. The rendition of the administration of the territory of Weihaiwei, as well as the transfer of public property in that territory and all other items to be transferred under this Convention, shall take effect on the date of the coming into force of this Convention.

Article 11. The National Government of the Republic of China shall, after the rendition of the administration of the territory of Weihaiwei, maintain, to the extent possible, the existing regulations, including those pertaining to land and property taxes, sanitation and building codes, and police administration.

Article 12. All legal deeds, sales, mortgages, and licenses issued to Chinese landowners by the British Weihaiwei Administration in accordance with the Weihaiwei Unoccupied Land Regulations No. 6 of 1919 shall, unless in conflict with Chinese laws and requiring modification or the issuance of new deeds, be deemed as valid as under British administration, subject to the conditions stipulated in the deeds.

Article 13. Foreigners holding land deeds issued in legal form by the former British Weihaiwei Administration shall be issued Chinese perpetual lease deeds, in the same format as the deeds recently issued by Chinese authorities to foreign landowners in the former British Concession in Zhenjiang. A registration fee of one yuan per mu shall be charged. The National Government of the Republic of China recognizes the validity of leases issued by the former British Weihaiwei Administration. If the National Government of the Republic of China decides to close the port of Weihaiwei, barring foreigners from residence and trade, in order to use it exclusively as a naval base, the Chinese Government agrees to compensate foreign owners and tenants for the recovery of their property interests at a fair price agreed upon by the two Governments. This price shall be negotiated item by item by a Joint Committee formed by representatives of the two Governments.

Article 14. The National Government of the Republic of China agrees to maintain existing public utilities. The personnel in charge of these utilities shall be chosen by the Chinese Government. Special attention shall be given to the telephone service on the mainland of Weihaiwei and its connection with the telephone service on Liu Kung Tao, as well as the telegraph service between the mainland of Weihaiwei and Liu Kung Tao and Chefoo.

Article 15. All cases adjudicated by the British High Court or District Court of Weihaiwei before the rendition shall be deemed to have the same validity as those adjudicated by Chinese courts after the rendition.

Article 16. The National Government of the Republic of China shall, before deciding to close the port of Weihaiwei and reserve it exclusively as a naval base, maintain the port as an international trade and residential area, including the present locations of all foreign owners and tenants.

Article 17. Before the enactment and implementation of a Chinese local self-government system, Chinese local authorities shall consult with the foreign community on municipal matters directly related to the well-being and interests of foreign residents in Weihaiwei.

Article 18. The National Government of the Republic of China shall, before deciding to close the port of Weihaiwei and reserve it exclusively as a naval base, lease certain properties in the area, as listed in Annex 2, gratuitously to the British Government for the use of the British Consulate and the public welfare of the residents, for a period of thirty years, which may be renewed upon expiration.

Article 19. All existing navigational facilities, such as lighthouses, buoys, and weather signals, shall be transferred gratuitously to the National Government of the Republic of China and maintained by the appropriate Chinese authorities in the future. The administration of the port shall be conducted in the same manner as other Chinese treaty ports.

Article 20. This Convention shall be ratified, and the instruments of ratification shall be exchanged in Nanjing on or before October 1, 1930, i.e., the first day of the tenth month of the nineteenth year of the Republic of China. This Convention shall come into force on the date of the exchange of ratifications. This Convention is made in duplicate, both copies of which are signed and sealed by the Plenipotentiaries of the two countries as evidence of their good faith. Done in Nanjing, this eighteenth day of April, in the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, corresponding to the eighteenth day of April, one thousand nine hundred and thirty.

Annex 1. Stored items to be returned to the Chinese Government, including the following items: a portion of the equipment in the residence, telegraph lines (island and mainland), one small launch "Alexander" and two small boats, electric poles and streetlights and storage related to streetlights of the British Weihaiwei Administration, sanitary vehicles, mules, and equipment, firefighting equipment, telephones, electric poles, insulators, wires, and switchboards, police uniforms (including those currently in use and in storage), various storage devices related to police affairs, bicycles, firearms, etc. (currently used by the police) and their ammunition, telephone lines (island and mainland).

Annex 2. List of land and buildings in Weihaiwei leased by the National Government of the Republic of China to the British Government. The residence of the Chief Chinese Secretary and its courtyard and horse stable are to be used as the residence of the British Consul in the future; the junior officers' quarters and courtyard are to be used for the British Consulate in the future; two foreign cemeteries, one in Edward Port and one on Liu Kung Tao; No. in the old barracks, for use as a British club. If the club is dissolved, the building shall be returned to the National Government of the Republic of China without compensation. As for the section of the old parade ground wasteland, both parties have agreed to continue its use as a public playground and baseball field as it is currently. If this land is needed for public welfare purposes, including the expansion of the seaport, the Chinese local authorities shall select an equally suitable location for a public playground and baseball field. Annexes A and B indicate the aforementioned land and buildings, etc., but the municipal cemetery on Liu Kung Tao is not included.

Agreement

The undersigned, authorized by their respective governments, have agreed upon the following articles:

Article 1. The National Government of the Republic of China agrees to lease to the British Government several buildings and conveniences on Liu Kung Tao in Weihaiwei Bay, as listed in the annex, for use by the British Navy as a summer resort and sanatorium, for a term of ten years. Upon expiration, the lease may be renewed with the same conditions or with other conditions agreed upon by the two governments. At the end of the lease term, all land, buildings, etc. shall be returned to the National Government.

Article 2. The National Government of the Republic of China agrees, to the extent possible, to properly maintain the existing municipal administration methods on Liu Kung Tao (i.e., roads, docks, police, sanitation, streetlights, etc.) and preserve the existing forests, prohibit the opening of brothels, and prohibit the sale of alcohol and narcotics, etc., except in licensed premises, and maintain the existing cultivation regulations on the island. The National Government undertakes to include a stipulation in the contract that all the above-mentioned articles must be observed when selling or leasing state-owned land and buildings on the island.

Article 3. (1) From early April to the end of October each year, British warships and auxiliary vessels are allowed to anchor in the anchorage dredged by the British Navy off Liu Kung Tao, provided that the Chinese Navy has priority of use. In the event of war involving Great Britain or the Republic of China, British warships and auxiliary vessels must immediately withdraw completely in accordance with international practice. (2) The British Navy shall enjoy the benefit of towing targets from the anchorage of Liu Kung Tao to the open sea for exercises, but shall pay due attention to fishermen's nets and avoid damage. (3) During the period of the British Government's use of the buildings and conveniences on Liu Kung Tao under Article 1 of the Tripartite Agreement,

Page 9

Brief News

After receiving the annual request from the British Navy through the Chinese authorities, it shall be approved. The British Navy shall enjoy the benefit of landing, drilling, and target practice on Liu Kung Tao, but if there is local unrest, the landing drills may be temporarily suspended after notification from the local authorities to the British Navy.

Article 4. All items needed by the British Navy shall be allowed to be imported, stored, loaded, unloaded, and transshipped in Weihaiwei in accordance with the customs and trade practices. The British Government declares that it will not store firearms or ammunition on Liu Kung Tao.

Article 5. All existing buoys and mooring facilities set up by the British Navy in Weihaiwei waters shall be transferred to the National Government of the Republic of China without compensation and shall continue to be maintained for the use of the British Navy, provided that the Chinese Navy has priority of use. All such buoys and mooring facilities may be moved at any time by the Chinese Navy or port authorities when deemed necessary.

Article 6. This Agreement shall be ratified, and the instruments of ratification shall be exchanged in Nanjing on or before October 1, 1930, i.e., the first day of the tenth month of the nineteenth year of the Republic of China. This Agreement shall come into force on the date of the exchange of ratifications. This Agreement is made in duplicate, both copies of which are signed and sealed by the Plenipotentiaries of the two countries as evidence of their good faith. Done in Nanjing, this eighteenth day of April, in the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, corresponding to the eighteenth day of April, one thousand nine hundred and thirty.

Annex. List of land and buildings on Liu Kung Tao leased by the National Government of the Republic of China to the British Government, and various conveniences allowed. 1. A baseball field and its buildings. 2. A sailor's rest teahouse. 3. Naval cemetery. 4. Naval village. 5. Junior officers' club and tennis court. 6. Sports ground for officers and soldiers, together with buildings and croquet, baseball, tennis courts, officers' court. 7. A portion of the hospital site and its buildings, the location of which is approximately south of the road passing through the center of the site, together with the Commander-in-Chief's tennis court, as marked on map A. 8. The Commander-in-Chief's Office (61) and nearby houses (62). 9. The joint army and navy club and garden (57). 10. Residences and gardens numbered (52), (54), (55), (58), (59), (60), (73) on the map. 11. Hospital (53) and its storeroom (50), hospital staff residence (49), and generator plant (51). 12. No. (70) and Nos. (30) to (40), and Nos. (75), (47), (48), (68), (29A) storerooms, and (29) two rooms sufficient to store 6,000 tons of coal. 13. The Royal Navy Tavern (temporarily leased until the National Government provides a suitable building to replace it). (Note) The numbers in parentheses are the numbers in Annex B. The following conveniences, land, and buildings are shared with the Chinese Navy. 1. Target range land and buildings. 2. Machine well (limited). 3. Iron dock. British Navy coal barges are also allowed to dock in the small dock, and coal workers are facilitated. As for the quarry to be returned in accordance with the Special Agreement for the Handover of Weihaiwei, the British Government may still extract stone materials from it when needed without charge. Annexes A and B indicate the aforementioned land and buildings, etc.

Important Military News between Xu and Yu 55

Enemy Forces in Yucheng and Xiayi Retreat Backwards

Rumors of Mutiny in Sun Dianying's Forces

A fast dispatch from Xuzhou states that according to military sources, the enemy's frontline troops in Yucheng and Xiayi suddenly began retreating backward on the first day of the month. Their plan to advance eastward on the third seems to have been altered again. However, their frontline mixed troops appear to be quite disorganized. Wan Xuancai, Sun Dianying, and others have been constantly sending representatives to Xuzhou to negotiate surrender, but it seems that this side does not attach much importance to it. Since General Commander Chiang issued a vow to suppress Yan and Feng on the first, the morale of the Central Army has been greatly boosted. The Central Army's front line in eastern Henan has been fully deployed, gaining the upper hand. They remain calm and composed, awaiting further orders. According to a reliable investigation of the enemy's front line, Wan Xuancai himself has arrived in Guide, Sun Chu's troops have also arrived in the Kaifeng and Lanfeng area, and Shi Yousan's troops are still in Kaocheng and Dongming. Sun Dianying's troops seem to be increasing towards Haozhou. It is said that Feng has appointed Sun Chu as the commander-in-chief, but the front mixed troops cannot be unified. The aviation team has been dispatching planes to patrol for days to destroy enemy defenses. It is reported that on the second, a large number of planes flew west and dropped eight bombs on Guide and Lanfeng, destroying one train of enemy vehicles at Guide Station and one transport vehicle at Lanfeng Station. The enemy is very panicked because the enemy's forward troops have no aircraft and have no way to resist the Central Army's aircraft. Central Army armored vehicles are continuously patrolling and defending the western route, and the road defense is extremely solid. The Xuyang passenger car runs smoothly as usual. According to another telegram from Fan Xixu, our aviation team has dispatched planes to fly west for days, bombing and injuring many of Shi's troops in Dongming and Kaocheng. Ye Kaixin also telegraphed that there was a mutiny in Sun Dianying's army in Haozhou, and many returned to their villages. The enemy's morale has collapsed. According to military observations, our army is absolutely confident in attacking. Many of the enemy's forward generals have expressed their willingness to surrender, which is particularly unfavorable to the enemy. Even if the Jin army joins the front, the combat effectiveness is quite lacking. The military situation in Xu and Yu should not be prolonged. (3rd)

Aftermath of the Xiamen Convenience Steamer Tragedy 56

Corpses and Relatives' Groups Established

Statements from the Party Department and Customs

A dispatch from Xiamen on the 28th states that the convenience steamship of the Quanxia Liaison Line Quanhe Automobile Company sank between Wutong and Aotou, killing passengers. It has been ascertained that 192 people drowned. Up to the most recent count, 158 bodies have been recovered. The joint meeting of the Party, government, and military decided to arrest the responsible person, but it has not yet been implemented. The resolution to have the relatives of the deceased file a lawsuit in court, requesting the sealing of the assets of the person in charge, is still under investigation. A group of relatives has been established and a committee for receiving the assets of Quanhe has been organized, but they are all in preparation. As for the Party, government, and military, they have handed this case over to the court for handling. The headquarters has not intervened. On the Party's side, the "Committee for Handling the Wutong Shipwreck Tragedy by the Party Departments of Various Counties in Southern Fujian," organized by the Party Departments of Siming, Jinjiang, Nan'an, and Hui'an counties, has issued a declaration stating that Quanhe Automobile Company is certainly fully responsible for this tragedy. Therefore, at 9:00 AM on the 11th, Comrades Chen Lianfen and Zhang Fubin of the Siming County Steering Committee went to the Xiamen Garrison Headquarters to see Commander Lin Guogeng and asked him to detain the persons involved in this case first and await handling. At that time, Commander Lin said that in order to be cautious, he would first send someone to investigate the truth and then handle it according to the circumstances. The judicial authorities have also not taken concrete action, so that the person in charge of the company is still at large, even publishing notices, saying nice things and confusing social rumors. The officials of the authorities are tolerant and considerate, which can be said to be meticulous, but we believe that this tragedy is not comparable to ordinary events. The Xiamen military, government, and judicial authorities, who live and eat here, should, in theory, make an emergency decision and quickly detain the persons involved in the tragedy and await trial. But now it is the opposite. No wonder there is a full stomach of doubts and complaints.

After this case occurred, the Party Department and various social groups sent letters to the Customs asking questions. Quanhe Company also claimed that the excess number of passengers was released after being checked by Liu Wudian Changguan. The Customs Superintendent issued a letter to the Chinese Council on the 25th, explaining Quanhe's violations and responsibilities. The original text is as follows: Directly replying, on the 16th of this month, the letter from Taiwan regarding the case of the convenience steamship of Quanhe Automobile Company causing disaster in Wutong Port was received, and the suggestions made were approved by this office to the Customs Commissioner, who replied that all ships registered in this Customs are inspected once a year. If the hull and machinery are not strong, they will be ordered to stop sailing. The convenience electric boat was inspected by this Customs on February 7 this year, and the hull and machinery were found to be suitable for use. Its tonnage is eight tons and zero forty-eight, and the Customs has limited the number of passengers to eighty-five, including sixty-four in the upper cabin and twenty-one in the lower cabin. It was found that this ship was sailing from Aotou to Wutong, and it actually carried more passengers privately beyond the number limited by the Customs in order to profit, so it sank between Ao and Wu, and did not sail to Liu Wudian, so Liu Wudian Changguan had no way to check. Before the accident, this Customs and its affiliated branches had repeatedly warned the ships not to carry more passengers than the limited number. Unexpectedly, the ship only cared about profit and disregarded danger, which led to the occurrence of this tragedy. Tracing back to the cause, it was all because of the ship's captain, and it was found that all foreign transport ships must first have lifebuoys prepared by the ship, and then limit the number of passenger berths according to the number, so there is one ring for each passenger, and even if there is danger, they can be rescued according to the number of people, but Chinese ships rarely have this equipment, so once there is danger, there is no way to deal with it. Now the ship has caused many deaths due to non-compliance with customs regulations, which is very regrettable. The shipowner should be held responsible. In addition to returning the original document, the letter is hereby replied for your information. The Xiamen Customs Supervision Office.

Songjiang 57

The County Government is Preparing to Welcome and Bring Back Lake Bandits On the 28th of last month, the town of Sijing was plundered by lake bandits, who fled in all directions. Thirty people were intercepted by Qingpu County in various places and handed over to the Qingpu County Government for questioning. After investigation, two merchants were found to be innocent. Among the remaining bandits were those who had participated in the Chonggu robbery case. County Magistrate Shen handled them separately. Yesterday, a note came from Songjiang, saying that 13 bandits related to the Sijing robbery case and one dead bandit had been captured. After investigation, it was confirmed that they were requesting the dispatch of police to bring them back for legal action. The local county government is preparing the procedures for welcoming and bringing back the bandits.

Cheap Tin Foil Sparks Controversy The Yuanheng Store, opened by the Shao gang in Bailongtangkou, specializes in tin foil and held a low-price sale starting on the 2nd of this month, and moved to the old site of Luyongshun. The Zhentai, Dingtai, and Jinwen paper stores of this gang also launched a low-price sale. At the same time, other paper stores that also operate tin foil have also risen up in response and distributed flyers to attract customers. The wording in the flyers caused a misunderstanding by the Yuanheng Foil Store, which also printed flyers and hired a military band to parade and distribute them, but there were many retorts in the wording. The local colleagues were angry after seeing it and have now asked the industry representatives to question the store. It is said that both sides have reported their reasons, and it may not be easy to resolve them at once.

Wuxi 58

Received Threatening Letter After Robbery The home of Zhu Pansheng in Zhuxiang Lane, Kaiyuan Township, Fourth District, was robbed of clothing and accessories worth more than 1,000 yuan on the night of the 30th of last month. Afterwards, a list of losses was filed and submitted to the county government for investigation. Unexpectedly, the Zhu family suddenly received a letter from the bandits a few days ago, stating, "This time, Mr. Zhu got a big advantage, but he reported it to the government and published it in the newspaper. We cannot forgive it. Now we still need to borrow thousands of yuan, otherwise we will deal with it with drastic measures." The Zhu family was panicked and didn't know what to do. The Detective Chief of the Water Police District and the Police Chief of the County Government went to the countryside yesterday to investigate and verify the traces for investigation.

Communist Arrested and Handed Over to the County Yu Jugen (also known as Aju), a famous communist in Yuxiang, Wuliuqiutu, under the county's jurisdiction, had gathered his accomplices last year to shoot and kill villager Xu Ayuan. The county government had issued an arrest warrant for him. Recently, Yu suddenly returned home, intending to sell his ancestral property to others. His wife, Yu Tao, expressed her opposition and earnestly advised her husband to oppose the Communist Party. Unexpectedly, Yu Jugen roared loudly, making a lot of noise. Yu Tao was extremely angry and went to the First Squadron of the police stationed in the township to report that her husband, Yu Jugen, was a communist and requested his arrest. After receiving the report, Squadron Leader Feng immediately led armed police officers to arrest Yu and took him back for questioning. He was handed over to the county police team for interrogation. Yu Jugen confessed that he was thirty-three years old and did not admit to joining the Communist Party. After his wife, Yu Tao, came to the case to testify, Yu finally lowered his head and said nothing. After the interrogation, he was handed over to the county for trial.

The Origin of the Black-Clad Gunshots According to the reports of Zhou Guotang, the Fourth District Chief, and Wang Hao and Yan Zongling, the heads of Yongfeng Tongle Township, gunshots and noisy voices were heard on the riverside coast on the night of the 18th of last month, suspected of being bandit police. Poor Weather Affects Wheat and Silk Since the beginning of spring, the weather has been poor, and the wheat and silk have been greatly affected. Water accumulates in the fields and does not go away, and the wheat has withered and yellowed. The wheat ears are beautiful but not real, and the harvest is expected to be poor. Silkworms have large bodies and the second sleep is born with inclusions, the fine sleep heads are uneven, and the leaf price has fallen to about one yuan. No one has asked about the cocoon industry yet.

Yangzhou 61

Continued Request for Verification and Issuance of Road Work Wages: The explicit decree stipulates that road work wages for road construction workers can only be issued in areas where more than 50% of the region has been affected by disasters. This year's autumn survey at the county level and above, though approved for a tax reduction of 2.4%, in reality the disaster damage exceeded 50%. Therefore, according to Article 6, Item 3 of the Finance Department's ordinance on disaster assessment and tax reduction, which states that for areas with more than 50% damage, 30% of taxes should be levied, a continued request has been submitted to the Construction Department, along with the relevant ordinance, requesting verification and issuance of road work wages. It is unknown whether approval will be granted.

Liu Qi: Diligent, cautious, and hardworking. Tao Hongru: Young, energetic, and handles matters prudently. Hu Min: Hardworking in assigned tasks. Yang Guoxiang: Simple and hardworking. Zhu Xuanxi: Talent still developing, diligent in work. Zhang Heng: More than capable in handling matters, but lacks talent.

Outcome of Financial Community Meeting: Representatives from the Suzhou-Shanghai-Zhenjiang money industry came to Yangzhou yesterday (the 3rd) to discuss relief measures for the Yangzhou financial sector. The Chamber of Commerce president, Wang Jingting, along with members of the Money Industry Association, repeatedly deliberated on relief measures. The result was to extend the maturity of loans of various local money shops (approximately 2 million taels) by three months and to use 200,000 yuan to stabilize the Yangzhou market. Consequently, the current situation has become more moderate, and there should be no further talk of bankruptcies.

Case of Beating Resulting in Death Reported for Investigation: In Shijiawei Village, Eastern Township, there lived Wang Yanshi's son, Wang Shenghua, who was naturally timid and weak. Local hooligans, including Li Yuebo, claimed that Wang was having an affair with Wang Xie, a woman from the same village, intending to extort money unsuccessfully. Yesterday afternoon, as Wang was passing by Tanjiapu Village, Li summoned a group of people to beat him severely. By the time Wang Yanshi heard the commotion and went to rescue him, he was already dead. A report was filed with the county government today (the 4th), and the county government has dispatched officials to conduct an investigation.

Jiaxing 62

Major Dispute over Fish Farming in Chengxi: A certain Jia, a resident of Shaoxing residing in Jiaxing's Youchegang, joined with local townspeople to initiate fish farming with staked enclosures in the Chengze and Liansi lakes near Chengxi in order to profit from fishing. However, this was opposed by local townspeople, who submitted a complaint to the provincial government. After review, the provincial government, in accordance with Article 5 of the Zhejiang Western Water Conservancy Prohibition Rules, ordered the county to stop the practice. Disregarding the provincial order, the fish farmers continued their activities, placing stakes in Liansi Lake recently in preparation for stocking. The people of Yang'an village nearby felt that this method would cut off the livelihood of the fishing households and therefore拔所所插之　, removed the stakes. This provoked the anger of the Shaoxing residents, who gathered a large group yesterday to beat the residents of Yang'an Village at their doorstep. The villagers also gathered a large group and seized three Shaoxing boats and detained three Shaoxing residents. Both parties have now filed lawsuits in court.

That you publish this letter to correct the record, in order to preserve your credibility. Thank you immensely. Respectfully, Feng Shiqing of Jiashan.

Anhui Department of Education Sets Date for Sending Students Abroad 65

Examination Date: July 5th

Anhui Province originally planned to send 14 students abroad at provincial expense. There are currently 7 vacancies. The types of students to be sent abroad this year are as follows: (1) One engineering student, limited to the following five departments: (a) Chemical Engineering, (b) Hydraulic Engineering, (c) Electrical Engineering, (d) Mining and Metallurgy Engineering, (e) Mechanical Engineering; (2) One medical student; (3) One natural science student, limited to the following three departments: (a) Chemistry, (b) Physics, (c) Biology; (4) One social science student, limited to the following five departments: (a) Political Science, (b) Economics, (c) Education, (d) Sociology, (e) Law. Any citizen of Anhui who has graduated from a national university or a registered university and has served for more than one year after graduation, or who has served as a professor or lecturer at a national university or a registered university for more than one year, may take the examination. A Review of the Second National Education Conference (9) 69

(7) Plan to Improve Higher Education

Higher education is planned to focus on enriching the content and raising the standards of existing universities during the six-year period of political tutelage. Only qualitative improvements will be made, and no quantitative expansion will be made. Efforts will be made to increase the number of students studying abroad and to establish specialized schools. Extra efforts will be made to allocate funds over ten years to encourage academic research.

(1) Measures to Enrich National Universities

(1) Supplementing construction: University classrooms, dormitories, and offices are mostly incomplete, and other general and special construction projects are even more lacking. Remedial measures include: A. The Ministry of Education will instruct national universities to consider the urgency of the situation and report the construction projects that need to be carried out, along with drawings and budgets. After investigation and approval, the Ministry of Finance will be notified to allocate temporary funds to each university for construction according to schedule. B. The Ministry of Education will instruct national universities to economize on regular expenses and transfer funds for construction, but this should not exceed 10% of the budget. C. National universities can raise private donations to carry out important construction projects. Donations of 1,000 yuan or more should be reported to the Ministry of Education for commendation.

(2) Expanding university equipment in preparation should be carried out simultaneously with construction. Currently, most national universities are poorly equipped. Remedial measures include: A. The Ministry of Education will formulate standards for the equipment of each college in the university and order each university to gradually expand according to the standards. B. It is stipulated that equipment fees should account for 30% to 40% of the university's budget, of which library fees should not be less than 20% for colleges of arts, law, commerce, and education, and not less than 10% for colleges of science, agriculture, engineering, and medicine. Instrument and specimen fees should not be less than 20% for colleges of science, agriculture, engineering, and medicine. C. Investigate the equipment expenses required by national universities that exceed 40% of the regular expenses, and transfer the funds to the Ministry of Finance to allocate temporary funds. D. Investigate which national universities need special scientific equipment, and request the China Cultural Education Foundation or other Gengkuan funds to provide subsidies.

(3) Reorganizing departments and courses: The University Organization Law stipulates that universities must establish at least one college, and each college should have departments. Except for the College of Medicine, which does not have departments, and the College of Law, which may have only a law department, the Colleges of Arts, Science, Education, Agriculture, and Commerce should each establish departments as the minimum requirement. Currently, national universities are self-governing and cannot be consistent. Reorganization measures include: A. National universities with less than three colleges should urgently increase the number of colleges within a limited time to meet urgent needs. National universities with three or more colleges need not increase the number of colleges temporarily within two years. They should increase the number of departments to enrich the content of each college. B. National universities that increase the number of colleges and departments should first start with equipment, prepare a budget, and submit it to the Ministry of Education for review and approval by the Ministry of Finance. National universities in the same region should avoid duplication when adding colleges and departments. Those that have already been duplicated should be merged within the possible range. C. The Ministry of Education should organize a committee to formulate curriculum standards for each college and department of national universities. Before the standards are formulated, each university should formulate its own curriculum and submit it to the Ministry for approval. This curriculum should focus on the main courses. Those that are required courses in Department A may be elective courses in Department B. There should be no disagreement, and courses with different names but the same content should not be established indiscriminately. In order to adapt to local conditions, special lectures on scientific aspects may be set up in addition to the prescribed courses. The expenses may be borne by the Ministry of Education, which will transfer them to the China Education and Culture Foundation or other Gengkuan funds. D. Students' course selection should be guided by the department head or professor, distinguishing between major and minor courses that are interrelated. They should not avoid difficult courses. The number of credits for each course should be stipulated in the curriculum standards.

(4) Improving teaching effectiveness: Currently, many university faculty and staff hold concurrent positions, and the average number of students taught per person is less than four. In terms of effectiveness, it is not economical. Measures to improve effectiveness include: A. Before the Ministry of Education implements the review of university faculty qualifications, national universities should carefully select and hire professors and lecturers in accordance with the regulations on university faculty qualifications. If there are no suitable talents in the country to take on the most important subjects, famous foreign scholars should be hired at high salaries, or they should be jointly hired by various schools to give lectures in rotation. B. National universities should appropriately increase the salaries of faculty members in accordance with the university faculty salary scale. Those who can devote themselves to research and writing may appropriately reduce the number of teaching hours. If funds are not very generous, unimportant subjects should be appropriately cut to concentrate the subjects. C. National universities should do their best to reduce staff and increase faculty members. Faculty members should be full-time in principle, and part-time faculty members should not exceed one-third of the total number. Faculty members from School A who also hold faculty or important positions at School B must be strictly prohibited. D. University professors and lecturers should have designated times to meet with students on campus outside of classroom teaching and be responsible for individual guidance. Those with teacher and student dormitories should promote and try out the tutor system. E. National university students should be valued for their quality rather than quantity, and attention should be paid to strict examinations and extracurricular assignments to enrich their knowledge and skills. F. National universities should successively establish research institutes or research centers.

(5) Determining and allocating funds: A. Salaries should account for 55% to 65%, of which faculty salaries should not be less than 45% and staff salaries should not exceed 10%. B. Equipment fees should account for 30% to 40%. C. Office expenses should account for 5% to 10%. D. Special expenses should not exceed 5%.

(2) Reorganize existing provincial universities and stipulate methods for increasing the location of universities

(1) Existing provincial universities should be reorganized in accordance with the University Organization Law and Regulations. Those that meet the regulations should be expanded according to the special needs of the local area. A. Shanxi University currently has departments of arts, law, and engineering, and should add a college of medicine. B. Chengdu University, Chengdu Normal University, and Sichuan University should be merged into one university, and colleges of arts, science, law, and education should be established based on the existing departments. A college of medicine will be added in the future. C. Hebei University currently has colleges of arts, law, agriculture, and medicine, and the Hebei College of Law and Commerce should be merged into it. D. Henan Zhongshan University should be renamed Henan University. Shaanxi Zhongshan University and Lanzhou Zhongshan University should first be reorganized into small-scale independent colleges, each with departments of arts and sciences, tentatively named Shaanxi College and Gansu College. If Guangxi, Guizhou, and Jilin Universities cannot comply with the regulations quickly, they should also be reorganized into independent colleges, each with departments of arts and sciences. E. Anhui University and Hunan University should be given a time limit to seek the need to fill the departments.

(2) In addition to the established national and provincial universities or colleges, the location of future universities should be determined by the Ministry of Education in accordance with the financial resources, environment, and requirements of each locality.

(3) All newly established universities should be called colleges when they are first established, with departments of arts and sciences. Only after three colleges are completed can they be called universities. In addition to colleges belonging to arts and sciences, they must be set up according to local needs. Before the colleges are set up, senior high schools should be set up.

(4) Provinces with or near national universities do not need to set up provincial universities.

A selection committee will be formed separately for evaluation. (3) Categories include calligraphy, painting, crafts, sculpture, photography, methods: individual, group, school, and other, which will be handled by the Solicitation Department. (4) Deadline for works: one month from May 1st. (5) Exhibition period: ten days from June 15th to 25th. (6) The venue will be handled by the Design Committee. (7) Shi Shangpeng will be responsible for drafting the exhibition regulations. (Education Society)

Results of the First Day of the Jiangnan University Games 75

Central Zhao Rugong's Long Jump Breaks National Record

Central Won All Five Finals Yesterday

Central and Jinan Will Strive for the Championship Today

The fourth Jiangnan University Sports Association Games began at 1:30 pm yesterday. The sun shone brightly that day, and the weather was warm, making it a good opportunity for track and field competitions. The number of spectators was still considerable. The order of the venue was maintained by Zhang Zijun of Guanghua, which was quite effective. Central won all five finals yesterday, which was not easy. It is now in the lead with 32 points, and the hope of winning the championship is quite high. Today's afternoon is all finals. In the pole vault, outstanding results are expected, and there will inevitably be fierce competition among the athletes from various schools to win the championship. The details are recorded below.

Far Eastern Tennis Championship 83

Japanese confident of victory

Our country's athletes must strive harder

Mr. Yashikawa, a prominent figure in Japanese tennis, wrote an article titled "Japan Can Win at the Games' Tennis" in the Sports World magazine published by the Sports Association. He discussed the strengths of the three countries in detail. Although his confidence may be excessive, it is still valuable for our reference. The translation is as follows:

Anyone who makes predictions about the Far Eastern Games' tennis championship

must not ignore the results of the Malani Carnival tennis competition this spring, as it was a competition to determine the Philippine representatives and can be considered a prelude to the Far Eastern Games. Not only Filipino players participated, but also players from Japan and especially from China, where Lin and Qiu were destined to meet in the Tokyo Games, and also Japan's Sato and Bui.

A decisive encounter

In the singles competition at that event, Japan's Sato and Bui easily won. At the Tokyo Games this month, those two will naturally be able to secure victory, and thanks to their singles wins, Japan can hope to achieve nine points of victory.

The doubles competition, however, is a different matter. Japanese players cannot be careless about this. The collaboration of the Filipino Alejo brothers is the best in the Philippines, and they defeated the Sato-Bui team at the carnival. Their strength should not be underestimated.

The Far Eastern doubles competition has always been a hard-fought battle. The Sato-Bui team attending from Japan cannot be considered the best. In terms of teamwork, the pairing of Shima and Yamagishi is superior. Japan will likely send the latter to seek revenge and wipe away the shame in this tournament. When the four powerhouses meet, there will certainly be a fierce battle. One could say that the excitement of the Games' tennis competition lies entirely in this battle.

What is the strength of the Philippines? In singles, the best is Alejo's younger brother, and Incha is second. According to recent news, they may not attend due to favorable conditions for attending. The third is Anbu, followed by Alejo's brother and Sanggesheng, who are evenly matched. Alejo's brother is very strong, but his technique is not consistent. As for doubles, the Alejo brothers are definitely Japan's strong rivals. If the Philippine Association cannot offer the brothers good terms despite a certain amount of expedition expenses, their substitutes would be the Anbu-Sanggesheng team, which is much weaker.

From the colony, China can send very outstanding players. Although this year's players don't seem very spirited, Mr. Lin has won championships in Australia, and Mr. Qiu has won championships in Singapore. The newcomers Jiang (Daozhang) and Wu (Shizhang) are also quite strong. Japan should remember its victory at the eighth Games, so it should also pay attention to Lin and Qiu. Otherwise, an unexpected loss is unavoidable, though it should not affect the championship.

In conclusion, Japan has never had players as strong as this year's. In terms of strength, it definitely has an absolute advantage among the three countries. Furthermore, since the Games are being held in Japan, Japanese players have an advantage. Teams traveling to a country with drastic changes in environment, if they compete without sufficient rest, will feel disadvantaged, whether it is the Philippines or China. In terms of climate, the impact on Chinese players is not as great as on the Philippine team. In Japan's colder climate, Filipino players may not be able to perform to their full potential. Therefore, as long as there are no major problems on Sato's side, the Japanese team can first defeat the Philippine army three to one, and then defeat China three to one or four to zero.

Japan is certainly very strong in the women's competition, but it is not guaranteed that they can win as easily as the men. Moreover, there are quite a few capable players among the Philippine players. Most likely, the governor's daughter, Miss Christie, will come. Although she lost in the Malani finals, she is a fairly good player.

The Chinese female players have not yet been determined. The two ladies, Li and Liang, who won in Hangzhou last month, both have considerable strength. Therefore, we must not repeat the mistake of the last time in Shanghai, where we only gathered some beautiful women and did not use skill as the standard.

On the Japanese side, in the singles competition, there are Nagohoshi Kobayashi Tomoko, Takiguchi Reiko of the Hahuku Club, and Iimura Toshiko. In the doubles competition, there is the Kobayashi-Asabuki team. All of them are experienced and strong players.

In summary, this championship belongs to Japan. China is not a concern for Japan. Japan's only opponent is the Philippines, and the only question is the margin of victory.

Strength of Japanese Women's Athletics 84

Indeed a formidable opponent for our country's representatives

Hoping that our country's athletes will pay special attention

Ms. Sun, Ms. Wu, and Ms. Feng, work hard

On April 27th and 28th, the Asahi Shimbun Company held the All-Japan Women's Athletic Games in Tokyo. Although this event is not related to the selection of athletes for the Far Eastern Games, all the results demonstrate the strength of Japanese women's athletics, which is worthy of attention by our people. According to the competition results, the best performer in the 100 meters was Ms. Muraoka, with a time of 13.5 seconds. The best in the long jump was Ms. Hitomi, with a distance of 5.68 meters, with other jumps of 4.80 meters and 4.76 meters. Ms. Hitomi is one of the world's top female athletes and holds many world records. The high jump was won by Ms. Kashima with a height of 1.38 meters, and Ms. Shimizu also reached 1.27 meters.

Davis Cup Tennis 86

Spain defeats Belgium

Australia defeats Switzerland

Jiji News Agency, Tokyo: In the Davis Cup tennis competition, the first match between Belgium and Spain resulted in Spain winning two and losing one. In the two singles matches held on the fourth, Spain won again, thus Spain won with a score of four to one. In the match between Australia and Switzerland, Australia had already won three consecutive matches, and the outcome was already decided. In the singles match in April, Australia won again, resulting in a victory of four to zero.

Press Association Warns Du Shu 87

For insulting reporters at the National Games

The Shanghai Journalists Association, regarding the incident of National Games referees Du Tingshu and Shu Hong insulting reporters, sent separate letters of warning to Du Shu yesterday. The original letter is as follows: Dear Sirs, according to reports from our members Yao Gengkui and others, the National Games were held in Hangzhou this time, and reporters from various Shanghai newspapers went to the event for coverage, working hard to promote it. However, referees Du Tingtong and Shu Hong abused their authority and publicly insulted reporters from Shanghai and Hangzhou newspapers at the venue, threatening to expel them. At the time, the reporters questioned them based on reason, and Du Shu, realizing they were wrong, asked Zhou Xiangxian, the deputy director of the Games organizing committee, to apologize on their behalf. The reporters prioritized the Games and did not want to pursue the matter further, but in order to maintain the close relationship between sports and journalism, it seems that this Association should issue a serious warning to Du Shu to prevent similar unfortunate incidents from happening in the future. After investigating the above report, this Association has found it to be true. This Association believes that your actions of insulting journalists

hinder the cooperation between the sports and news communities, which is regrettable. We are sending this letter of advice and hope that you will pay attention and abide by the principle of mutual assistance and cooperation in the future and refrain from discourteous behavior and causing disputes. We sincerely hope for this.

National Far Eastern Table Tennis Preparatory Players 90

The preparatory office of the China National Table Tennis Federation held a meeting yesterday and the day before yesterday at the Great China Restaurant. Six preparatory committee members attended, including Lin Zecang, Zhang Yongchu, Wang Xiawen, Yu Binqi, Wang Mengnian, and Wu Maoqing. Chairman Lin Zecang reported that the Far Eastern Table Tennis Competition would be held in Japan and that the deadline was approaching, so a decision should be made on how to proceed. After discussion, the following decisions were made: (1) Seven athletes and one staff member will be sent. (2) Registration will be open from the 5th to the 12th, with a three-day extension for out-of-town players. (3) The preliminary rounds will begin on the 13th. (4) Due to time constraints, the competition will initially use an elimination format, followed by a single round-robin system to select the athletes. (5) The registration fee is one yuan per person, and the registration address is the All-China Preparatory Office, c/o Mr. Lin Zecang, Sanhe Company, No. 20 Nanjing Road. (6) Fundraising will be carried out through special donations and the sale of spectator tickets. Special donations will be sought from those who are enthusiastic about sports to support the team's trip to the East. At the same time, donations will be sought from sports organizations to support the effort.

B｜That woman is my wife.

Escort｜Well, at least you won't be coming back. We still have to brave the heavy rain to return.

A Record of Sights and Sounds in Wenzhou, You. 93

My friend, Mr. Tang Ruogu, after marrying the famous dancer Ms. Li Ying, went to Wenzhou with Mr. Xu Xinbo, the president of the art society, and his new father-in-law, Mr. Tang Yuchi, to develop industries. It has been two months since they left. Yesterday, I received the third letter from the newly married couple and Mr. Xu, detailing their observations in Wenzhou. I have recorded some of them below.

Local language: The Wenzhou dialect is like Cantonese. It is easier to learn than Cantonese. However, many of its sounds are quite similar to English. It is quite ingenious and also laughable. For example, "no" is pronounced by Wenzhou people as "nuo," which is no different from the English word "NO." In addition, "completely" is read as ALL, and "see" is read as SEE. They all match the English pronunciation. It is also a good material in Chinese linguistics.

Single angle: Recently, single silver corners can be said to have completely disappeared in Shanghai. However, single corners are much more prevalent in Wenzhou. Double corners are rare. All shops and entertainment venues use single corners. Every dollar can be exchanged for eleven corners and fourteen or fifteen copper coins. This is different from the situation in Shanghai.

Bo Ou: The largest department store in Wenzhou is located in Zhongshi on Wuma Street. The store is called Bo Ou. It has built a three-story Western-style building. The area is not even as large as the Lihua Company in this city. The imported European and Western goods have the flavor of being simple and crude. Therefore, the fashionable girls of Wenzhou are still considered behind the times in the eyes of Shanghainese.

Songs: Since last spring, each primary school in Wenzhou has added a singing class. More of the songs taught were by Mr. Li, with "Because of You" and "Grape Fairy" being the most common. However, most cowboys hum the song "Poor Qiuxiang". There are not many views of other songs, such as "Little Painter" and "Seven Sisters Visiting the Garden."

Street Fu: There is a custom in Wenzhou called Intercepting Street Fu. It is said that every street has fortune. Only by intercepting it for oneself can it be effective. Therefore, every household regards this as a kind of common sense, Chen Tiqiang.

Watching movies is better from a distance than up close. From a distance, the light is small and clear. From up close, the light is large and blurry, and the closer you get, the stronger the light, which damages your eyes. When paying the rickshaw puller in silver coins, it is best to ask the puller to see clearly in front of you. Because cunning pullers often replace them with inferior lead coins when passengers leave in a hurry, and then chase after them to exchange them. Many people are fooled by this.

Villains who set up gambling stalls to lure pedestrians are often seen in remote places along the road. You can also see many winners. In fact, they are all of the same ilk. Once you're hooked, you're done for.

If your teeth bleed when brushing, try using cold water to avoid this. Blood flows when it encounters heat and congeals when it is cold. Therefore, cold water has a hemostatic effect in an invisible way.

When reading books or newspapers, do not be too close to the object. Being too close reduces the possibility of long-distance sight and will naturally make one nearsighted over time, even if they were not so before.

When starting a watch, there should be a fixed time. For example, if it starts at a certain time today, it should also start at the same time tomorrow. The number of revolutions should also be fixed at start. Not too much, not too little. Too much reduces the elasticity of the regulations, and too little inevitably leads to stagnation along the way.

Essential work is highly valued. Many upper-class figures also participate. It is beautifully called the Social Entertainment Association. This association is held every day for a month, starting from the beginning of March each year. Lanterns are hung and decorations are colorful and dazzling, and there are various entertainments to add to the fun, such as puppet shows, Wenzhou opera, Beijing opera, blind singers, and Western music bands. The period of "intercepting street Fu" during this month is the most appealing to the people of Wenzhou. These games are almost always played every night. Therefore, local residents all dress in red and green, competing to dress up, and open their doors to allow people to visit, and they make novel arrangements to compete with each other. These kinds of situations are similar to the Dajiao celebrations in July and the New Year scenes in this city. The business of hawkers is ten times more profitable.

A Record of the Tragic Seven Deaths in the Guo Residence: Ms. Han Ying 94

Last month, on the 25th, a tragic massacre of seven lives occurred overnight at the Guo residence on Avenue Haig (now Huaihai Road). It was truly an unprecedented tragedy in Shanghai. I have a long-standing friendship with the Guo family, and what I have heard and seen is perhaps more accurate than what is known to the outside world. I am writing this account specifically. Readers, please do not regard it as ordinary writing. You must know that the background of this account is all marked with blood and tears.

Afraid to See the Little Dog: Guo's eldest daughter lived in the French Concession. A month ago, she bought a small dog, intending to give it to her mother as a pet. On the eve of the tragedy, her mother and Guo Song'an, now identified as the murderer, dined at her daughter's house. Song'an was good at judging dogs. Everyone asked him to evaluate it. He lifted the dog by the neck twice, examining all parts and checking its sex. I was also present at the time. Who knew that a great disaster would suddenly occur the next evening? Now everyone in the family is afraid to see this dog. It evokes memories of the scene and adds to the sorrow. They are even more afraid that the dog will remind them of the murderer's demeanor at the time.

Nurturing a Tiger to be Harmed: The Escaped Maid, Chonggui, was not originally raised by the Guo family. In 1925, Guo's daughter-in-law, Liu Yanqiu, gave birth to her eldest son, Susheng, on the occasion of his one-month celebration. Liu's mother brought the maid from Macau to Shanghai to accompany Susheng in the Guo residence. When the maid was young, her whole family suffered a bandit attack, and her parents were killed. Later, Liu's master, Quan Zhong, was ordered to suppress the bandits and rescued the maid from the tiger's den. The maid, being lonely and helpless, was fostered by Liu. The whole family treated her kindly. Unexpectedly, an unprecedented disaster arose from her. Alas, nurturing a tiger to be harmed has been true since ancient times. What can be done?

The Letter Arrived When the Person Died: Among the seven victims were two maids, one older and one younger. The older one, named Chunlian, died most tragically. In addition to the knife marks on her face and neck, her left hand was also severed, most likely due to resistance during the attack. Before her death, she had asked the Moonlight Company for a copy of the "Fashion Guide." Fearing that other maids would compete to read it, she used a pseudonym and had it sent to the Dunqi family. At the same time, she wrote a letter to inform the Guo family. Her intentions were truly good. How could she have known that the day the letter arrived would be the day the maid's body lay lifeless? Alas.

Dying with Eyes Wide Open: Guo's mother, Li Qiong'uan, and her daughter-in-law were both gentle and virtuous. Last year, the eldest daughter was engaged. Guo's mother then relinquished her duties of managing the household, entrusting all matters, large and small, to her daughter-in-law. She would then burn incense, light candles, practice vegetarianism, worship the Buddha, or teach the maids to read and write, and play with the grandchildren. Those who knew her all considered her a model matriarch. But now, she too could not die a peaceful death. If she has knowledge in the afterlife, I know that she would die with her eyes wide open.

Anecdotes about Banknotes: Qiu·Lang· 95

Banknotes are credit securities for the circulation of currency in society. Examining their system, they originated from the Jiaozi and Huizi of the Southern Song Dynasty. Initially, they were only regarded as salt and tea vouchers. As they were used for a long time, they were used as money. In the past, they were all issued by the government. Only recently have larger banks issued them. On the Bund of Shanghai, known for its prosperity, the variety of Chinese and foreign banknotes is too numerous to list. Here are some interesting anecdotes about banknotes to amuse readers.
