Travels in Southeast Asia (25): Sacred Flower 96

The eighth day. Gave a lecture at the National Language School. Mr. Ke Dawen from Fujian came specifically to promote the National Language Unification Movement. I strongly support this because there is a major obstacle here: there are many small groups that cannot be unified. Each group is based on its own dialect and runs its own schools. It is difficult to gather for events. This is also because the lack of a common language divides their strength. However, I believe that if the hundreds of temples here could have idle monks first learn the national language and then unite to give lectures every week, and also teach the common people to read, then in a few years, it would not only raise the cultural level of the Chinese but also spread Buddhism to the local people. Wouldn't that be a great thing? Unfortunately, most monks are illiterate and do not understand what Buddhism is. A few monks only recite scriptures and worship idols to gain alms from illiterate women. Alas. I think that Catholicism also originally worshipped idols, just like monks. Since Luther changed to destroy temples and remove idols, and lay preachers (Martin Luther Married Cathrine Bira), it has become today's Christianity, using scientific methods and approaching society. Because there are no idols to guard, pastors and their wives must use science to engage with society and build a society that assimilates with humanity. Monks, because they have temples and idols to guard, can earn alms that people naturally send, and thus become lazy and no longer care about the world, resulting in a hypnotic superstition. The harm of temples and idols to the development of Buddhism means that the image law must be eliminated. Baiwen established the Sangha system to teach and transform the community, but today's lack of progress is also due to this. Truly, advantages and disadvantages are born together, and it is not easy to discuss.

On the ninth day, I want to study some of the strange customs here. First, it is extremely hot here, but many people wear felt hats, the kind that Shanghai people wear in winter. Second, very few people carry fans. Third, according to Cantonese custom, when guests arrive, they rarely offer a washbasin and towel to greet them. This is also the case here. Fourth, because it is hot here, drinking tea is very important. But people here use extremely small teacups everywhere, about the size of wine glasses, to serve guests. After drinking, they pour again. This is not economical in terms of time. I find these four things very strange, and after much research, I could not find the reason. Later, I realized that people rarely carry fans because the slope land has a lot of wind, constantly day and night. But when you go to a small shop, it is still hot. It should also be because of a lack of promotion. There are also many people selling fans in the market, but few people use them. The locals told me, "Those born in the heat do not know the heat. You are worrying too much." I learned that the habit of drinking tea with small cups originated from the fact that the Min people are very particular about tea tasting. To respect guests, they use a small teapot placed in a porcelain dish, with two small cups. All are very exquisite. Each person has a teapot and two cups that they can pour and drink themselves, so it does not seem wasteful. Over time, it has become a public teapot with small cups for pouring, which is too clumsy. This is a case of misinformation leading to great inconvenience. This custom of tea tasting is very valuable. Japan learned from the people of Fujian. But there is one interesting thing: an addiction to tea tasting can also ruin one's family, even more than opium. Tea addicts use very expensive tea, several yuan per ounce, and gather with friends day and night to drink it, leading to the ruin of families worth ten thousand gold. It is also laughable. In all things, nothing should be excessive. Therefore, Confucius spoke of the Doctrine of the Mean, and Aristotle spoke of the Golden Mean. But today, people who do not have tea habits still use expensive tea with small teacups, which is a great mistake. Moreover, the porcelain is not from Jiangxi, and the cups are also inferior. They should be improved urgently. It is very hot here, but towels are not used to serve guests. Some say they are afraid of spreading germs, because Cantonese customs fear leprosy. But I always think it is neurotic. A friend who has been here for a long time says that it has become a habit and they don't notice it. However, there is one good thing: because there is wind here, the sweat stops after sitting for a short time. Only the matter of wearing felt hats in the tropics is incomprehensible. But since I have come to this place, I have no choice but to wear them because there are no straw hats anywhere. Westerners wear thick, white hats. In short, all four of the above matters should be reformed. First, felt hats should be replaced with straw hats. Second, people should carry fans. Third, towels should be offered to guests. Fourth, tea must be drunk with large cups. This should be done using a promotional method. Perhaps then it will be possible.

smoking. He had run out of paper cigarettes, and because it was late at night, there was nowhere to buy them. The young master was angry and took out several ten-yuan banknotes from his pocket, rolled them up and used them to smoke. He looked around to show off his extravagance, which made onlookers look askance.

Since the issuance of banknotes, people have found them lightweight and easy to carry, so they are actually used in transactions. However, the country bumpkins have simple ideas. Whenever they encounter a transaction, they must have hard currency. Most of them are unwilling to accept banknotes. It has even been said that those who use banknotes in our cities are regarded as people in the ledger of ghosts, which is so absurd that it is laughable.

On banknotes, one often sees idlers scribbling randomly, which is annoying. However, there are also poems and proverbs written on the blank edges of the banknotes, satirizing, scolding, and expressing everything. However, the banknotes are cold and indifferent, which cannot be denied. No wonder poor scholars complain.

The Exchange Rate in Shanghai Falls Due to Influx of Capital 98

Foreign Banks Close Early for the Horse Races

Yesterday was the day of the foreign Spring Horse Races. Foreign banks closed for half a day as usual, and some Chinese banks also closed. Therefore, the market was sluggish. As for the reason for the decline in the Shanghai exchange rate, it was only because the funds that merchants had previously sent to buy tea and miscellaneous grains were now being returned to Shanghai, resulting in an oversupply in the market. As a result, the rate fell every day. Yesterday afternoon, it had already fallen to within 0.02, with the morning rate at 0.072 and the afternoon rate at 0.071975, which was 0.00075 weaker than the morning rate of the previous day. The overnight money market was clearly in good order. All surplus funds were used to offset overdrafts, except for those needed by customers. Therefore, the money market slightly rebounded, and the overnight money rate immediately rose. Yesterday morning it was 0.014, and in the afternoon it was 0.012. The amount of remittances made was 1,081,000 in the morning and 1,285,000 in the afternoon. The amount of banknotes in the morning was 20,000, and there was no activity in the afternoon. The amount of banknotes in the outside market was 122,000 in the morning and 79,000 in the afternoon. The amount of silver dollars in the morning was 145,000 and 175,000 in the afternoon. Bank transactions amounted to 600,000 in the morning. In the afternoon, due to the holiday, there was little activity. The receipts and payments between foreign bank accounts were over 800,000, and the inflow and outflow of banknotes were over 1,000,000. The receipts and payments of silver dollars were not covered due to the closing of banks in the afternoon. The receipts and payments of foreign bank drafts by money shops were over 5,700,000, and the receipts and payments of silver bank drafts were over 31,000,000. The amount of foreign currency drafts was over 1,200,000, and the amount of silver currency drafts was over 2,400,000. The amount of foreign currency borrowing was over 500,000. Interest Rate for April is Two Taels 99

The interest rate for last month (April) has been decided recently. The interest rate is 2.95 taels, and the overdue interest is added according to the base rate of 4.5 qian. Therefore, the highest overdue interest is only 10.05 taels.

Reasons for the Decline in Silk Cocoon Shipments 100

This year, the total amount of silver dollars shipped out of Shanghai for the purchase of silk cocoons is less than four to five million, which is less than half of the previous years. There are several reasons for this decline: (1) People's hearts are not as good as in the past, and bandits are rampant. Cash is often robbed on the way. Recently, it was heard that a large batch of cash from a silk factory in Xibu bound for Hankou to buy cocoons was robbed, resulting in huge losses. Generally, cocoon merchants do not dare to take the risk. Therefore, recently, silver dollars that have already been purchased are being returned, resulting in an extremely cold and unusual cocoon market. (2) The silkworm production in various ports is generally not good, either due to the silkworm eggs, the cold weather, the war, or the feeding of the leaves. The overall results are not satisfactory anywhere. Therefore, many cocoon kilns have not been rented out, and many cocoon merchants have not arrived. This has caused the farmers who raise silkworm cocoons to complain bitterly. (3) The financial sector is unwilling to lend money for the preparation of funds for cocoon merchants. As a result, those who want to engage in this business are unable to obtain capital and can only listen helplessly. Recently, it has been heard that cocoon funds in various places are often robbed, and the risks are worrying. Most people dare not take the risk. Even those who are bold enough to do it cannot do so because the financial sector is unwilling to lend money rashly. Therefore, the market has become deserted.

The Continuing Sharp Decline in Bond Prices 104

Trading Reaches 11.5 Million Yuan

Yesterday, the bond market in Shanghai was very quiet in terms of spot transactions. The futures market, however, saw significant fluctuations in bond prices, leading to very active trading. The biggest price swings were related to issues such as consolidation, demobilization, and tariff adjustments. At the start of the morning, strong selling pressure caused bond prices to fall sharply. The selling pressure remained dominant throughout the morning and afternoon sessions, leading to the weakest market prices. These prices were about two yuan lower than the previous week. Later, market sentiment stabilized somewhat, and the selling pressure eased slightly. At the same time, there was a slight increase in buying to cover positions, which caused prices to fluctuate higher. As a result, compared to the previous week, besides the 96 Finance bonds, which remained mostly unchanged, consolidation and demobilization bonds continued to fall by about one yuan. Other bonds fell by amounts ranging from five to seven cents. Spot transactions for the entire day totaled only 15,000 yuan, while futures transactions reached 11.5 million yuan. Among futures, tariff bonds accounted for the largest share, totaling over 3.3 million yuan. Consolidation bonds reached over 2.6 million yuan, Rehabilitation bonds totaled about 1.7 million yuan, Continued Big Bonds 560,000 yuan, Continued Rolled Bonds over 800,000 yuan, and Demobilization bonds about 500,000 yuan. 96 Finance bonds amounted to over 200,000 yuan, while 7-year Finance bonds remained very quiet.

Gradual Expansion of Yarn and Cotton Yarn Sales 105

The yarn market was weak in the morning but rose in the afternoon. Actual yarn sales are expanding, and both Sichuan and Guangdong merchants are showing strong buying interest. If actual sales can continue uninterrupted, there should be a chance for prices to rise. However, overseas cotton yarn market conditions are generally trending downward, so most retail investors are inclined to sell. The rise and fall of the yarn market will depend on sales volume.

In the afternoon session, spot sales drove up the futures yarn market. The market opened lower in the morning due to the weakness of overseas cotton, and the market sentiment was weak. Retail investors sold off, with prices falling by two, three, or four cents across all months. However, trading volume was very low. In the afternoon, news that Sichuan and Guangdong merchants were purchasing spot yarn in large quantities tightened the market, and there were quite a few short covering trades. Prices rebounded by three, five, or six cents across all months. Total trading volume for the day was 9,600 bales. The closing prices for the afternoon session are listed on the left.

Speculation in near-month East Cotton contracts, rumors of large-scale deliveries, and an increasingly weak market situation in the current month have caused panic among retail investors, leading to a decline in market prices. However, the stance of the Hubei merchants remains strong, and they refuse to change their position.

Overseas Telegrams on Silk and Tea Show No Change 109

Yesterday's telegram on Chinese silk showed no change. Chinese merchants adopted a passive attitude. Silk Cocoon Merchants Meet to Discuss Saving the Cocoon Market 110

Unrest Persists in Various Regions, Many Cocoon Firms Cancel Leases

Result: No Progress

The spring cocoon season in various regions of Jiangsu and Zhejiang is approaching. However, due to rampant banditry in various regions, silk cocoon merchants dare not travel to collect cocoons with cash. In addition, unfavorable weather conditions have led to poor cocoon yields, and sluggish overseas silk sales mean that fresh silk is still being sold off at low prices. As a result, most of the cocoon firms that had leased cocoon trading houses have temporarily declared their cancellation of leases, causing widespread panic among cocoon trading houses in various regions. Therefore, they came to Shanghai the day before yesterday to invite silk cocoon merchants to hold a joint meeting to discuss solutions. The result was that, given the current situation, they made no progress. The Silk Cocoon General Association and the Silk Mill Trade Association have sent telegrams to the National Government, outlining the dire state of the silk cocoon industry, requesting that measures be taken to provide relief and maintain the industry.

Continued Opening of Sui'an Green Tea 111

Yesterday, the tea market for foreign firms in Shanghai was quite lively. Several hundred chests of new Zhenmei green tea samples produced by local tea factories have been launched on the market. Among them, Sui'an tea was opened by Tongfu Foreign Firm at a top price of 104 taels, about five or six taels lower than last year. Although the overall market sentiment was not too bad, only Tongfu Foreign Firm showed strong buying interest among the British firms. The rest mostly adopted a wait-and-see attitude. According to observations by general tea merchants, it is feared that the market will be difficult to sustain.

Stagnant and Weak Sales in Grain and Rice Market 112

About ten ships arrived at Zhabei yesterday. Sales were limited, with only a few top-grade Japonica varieties selling briskly. Second-grade Zhongguan Japonica was extremely sluggish, and the goods have been unowned for a long time, making them even less desirable. Although there were several transactions throughout the day, prices had to be lowered by half to two jiao. Supplies of late-season Bo rice were scarce, and sales remained sluggish. Large quantities were slightly reduced. Transactions in Yangdu and other top-grade varieties were few. General-grade rice was slightly inquired about by customers. Retail sales were very slow, and buying interest in Yinyuan rice was also quiet. The trend for Baiyuan rice was quite flat.

A small amount of rice arrived in the Hunan River area of Shanghai, and market conditions were generally flat. Stores showed strong interest in Changzhou and Wuxi Japonica, but lower grades were sluggish. Prices were high and stable, while lower grades were soft. Sales of Suzhou and Tongxiang machine-milled rice were average, and there was no significant buying interest from rural areas. Prices varied slightly. The situation for early-season Bo rice from southern counties was turning stable due to slow arrivals and sales. Prices remained unchanged. Small quantities of Yangdu top-grade rice arrived. Local stores selectively purchased them, and the market showed neither prosperity nor decline. Demand for Baiyuan rice was weak, and inventories remained high, resulting in a weak market trend. Prices were also high and flat, while lower grades were discounted.

Active Flour Sales, Prices Rising 113

Significant Increase of 1.75 Cents Recently

Yesterday, the flour market suddenly experienced a sharp increase this month. It is currently the off-season, and price fluctuations depend entirely on actual sales. If the sales do not pick up, the high market value will naturally be short-lived. Otherwise, if demand increases, the market will inevitably surge again. It was evident in the previous week that prices would not fall further this month. In terms of sales to the north, Tianjin needs 40,000 to 50,000 bags per day (yesterday's price was 3.685 yuan). Before the off-season, Shanghai flour had sales of one million bags. Nanjing and the Yangtze River area are buying flour for military use or to meet demands caused by rice shortages. Therefore, as sales have picked up, manufacturers have raised prices, which is expected. As a result, standard opening prices had to be raised sharply. However, based on the current situation, prices will not exceed five cents to a guan, as manufacturers are only seeking to cover costs and do not want to burden the people. As a result, the highest increase this month was 2.4725 taels, before falling slightly. Compared to the previous week, prices were up 1.75 cents. Forward-month contracts were showing positive trends, with June at 5 cents, July, August, and September at 2.5 cents, and October not yet opened.

Spot Wheat Trading at 13,000 Bags 114

Yesterday, wheat futures generally fluctuated within a range, showing a slightly weaker trend. This was due to the weather turning clear again, and foreign wheat prices were reported to be lower by two, three, or four jiao. Therefore, market sentiment was generally sluggish. However, traders from inland regions remained firm. Therefore, although there was an opportunity to push prices lower, the extent of the decline was limited. As a result, the June contract was down slightly by two fen compared to the previous weekend, the July contract was unchanged, the August contract was down slightly by one fen, and the September and October contracts were unchanged. Spot wheat supplies remained abundant due to continued arrivals, and prices trended stable. However, sales remained brisk due to better flour sales. Qingjiangpu, South Xuzhou, Xuzhou, and Bengbu wheat were priced at 4.92 taels, and Henan wheat was priced at 4.4 taels, with a total of over 13,000 bags traded. Fufeng and Shenda bought 3,500 bags, and the rest was bought by Fuxin.

Yesterday's Commemoration 119

General Manager's Inauguration Anniversary Meeting

Attended by Over a Thousand Representatives from All Sectors

Various Agencies Also Held Separate Events

Commemoration Activities Across All Sectors

Yesterday marked the 9th anniversary of the inauguration of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the General Manager of the Chinese Nationalist Party, as the Extraordinary President in Guangzhou. The Shanghai 5/5 Anniversary Commemoration Committee convened a meeting of representatives from all sectors at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce at 9:00 AM. The meeting was attended by thousands of party members and representatives from all sectors. As it was Monday, the expanded weekly memorial service was held first, with Fan Zhengbo as the chair and Xu Yefu as the master of ceremonies. After the ceremony, music was played to open the meeting, chaired by Chen Dezheng. Representatives from the Municipal Executive Committee, Pan Gongzhan, Dong Hangbai, and Lu Jingshi, delivered speeches in succession. The details are as follows:

Meeting Agenda: (1) Opening, (2) Music, (3) Singing of the Party Song, (4) Bow to the National Flag and the Portrait of the General Manager, (5) The Chairman Respectfully Reads the General Manager's Will, (6) Silent Tribute, (7) Chairman's Report, (8) Speech by the Representative of the Municipal Party Department, (9) Speeches, (10) Slogans, (11) Music, (12) Adjournment.

Meeting Chairman (Presidium): Zhang Qun, Chen Dezheng, Pan Gongzhan, Fan Zhengbo, Wang Yansong, Tong Hangbai, Ma Zhiying, Lu Jingshi.

Chairman's Report: Chairman Chen Dezheng delivered the opening remarks, stating that the party comrades have designated this day as an eternal memorial day for the party and the country. There are several points we should recognize on this memorial day. First, the environment on that day was dangerous and difficult, and the General Manager rose from that dangerous environment and fought against it. Looking at our current environment, it is no less dangerous than it was on that day. Do our comrades want to commemorate the General Manager by learning his fearless spirit to save the nation and the country from danger? This is the first point to explain. Second, many warlords like Ge Feng are stirring up trouble to satisfy their desires. In the past, the Beiyang warlord Wu Peifu was the representative, and now it is Ge Xishan and Feng Yuxiang. Do we want to awaken the people and unite the revolutionary masses to eliminate the current Beiyang warlords Ge Xishan and Feng Yuxiang? This is the second point. Third, Chen Jiongming communicated with the Beiyang warlords, hindering the General Manager, which led to Chen Jiongming's rebellion. The reason why the General Manager's Northern Expeditions failed several times was not because the revolutionary forces were weaker than the northern forces, but because counter-revolutionary forces were lurking within the revolutionary forces. Now, these counter-revolutionary forces are clearly represented by Wang Zhaoming, Chen Gongbo, Xie Chi, Xiang Lu, and others. Do we want to awaken the people and unite the masses to eliminate these counter-revolutionary elements? This is the third point. The most important significance of commemorating the General Manager's inauguration as the Extraordinary President is that we hope everyone will learn the General Manager's fearless spirit to eliminate the Beiyang warlords and save our country. Secondly, we need to explain that today the counter-revolutionary Communist Party is also commemorating the birthday of their ancestor Karl Marx. Today, our memorial day also happens to coincide with this counter-revolutionary memorial day. Our purpose is to save our nation and enable our nation to survive freely and independently, and not to become appendages of red and white imperialism. What we are doing today is not only saving the nation but also building democracy and people's livelihood. Everyone should recognize that the Communist Party does not want a nation. When we commemorate the General Manager who fought for the nation, we use our strength to eliminate the Communist Party, which is against the interests of the nation. Therefore, when we commemorate the General Manager's inauguration as the Extraordinary President, we must strive to eliminate the Beiyang warlords, save the country and the nation, and also eliminate the Communist Party, which is against the interests of the nation. This is the most important significance of today's commemoration. I hope all comrades will continue the General Manager's fearless spirit and work hard to make China truly free and equal so that compatriots can live and work in peace. The report is complete.

Speeches by Representatives: Speeches by Pan Gongzhan, Tong Hangbai, Lu Jingshi, and others representing the Municipal Party Department are omitted.

Leaflets: Leaflets distributed at the meeting included the Municipal Executive Committee's "Letter to Comrades Commemorating 5/5," "Letter to the People," the "5/5 Commemoration" booklet, the 5/5 Revolution Anniversary Commemoration Committee's "Commemorating 5/5" leaflet, and various colored slogans. After the meeting, they went to major streets throughout the city to distribute them.

Meeting Slogans: (1) Continue the General Manager's fearless spirit, (2) Eliminate the remaining Beiyang warlords, (3) Down with Yan Xishan and Feng Yuxiang, (4) Wipe out the Chinese Communist Party, (5) Down with imperialism, (6) Create a clean government, (7) Strive for political tutelage and construction, (8) Consolidate the revolutionary foundation, (9) Long live the Chinese Nationalist Party, (10) Long live the Republic of China.

To Be Signed in Beijing Today

Hong Kong Merchants Manipulating 122

Shanghai-Hong Kong Exchange Rate

Total Amount Reaches 200 Million Taels

Wenhui Bao reports that according to Hong Kong press reports from reliable sources, speculation in Shanghai-Hong Kong exchange rates has been rampant recently. Several Hong Kong merchants are extremely well-informed about exchange market news. Recently, they suddenly made large-scale purchases, totaling as much as 200 million taels. It is difficult to predict the future trend of the exchange market, but it can be said that there will be changes soon that will prevent these speculators from taking such risks in vain. However, with the sharp drop in the silver market, various sectors have already been greatly affected. If speculators continue to manipulate the market, the future may be even more unimaginable, which is truly unfortunate for the industrial and commercial sectors.

Customs Official Talks About Shanxi's Yan Xishan's Tax Interception 123

Hoping He Will Know the Opportunity and Stop

Yan Xishan's interception of Tianjin customs duties has aroused opposition from all circles, both Chinese and foreign. Now, according to a senior official of the Inspectorate General of Customs, this matter is also mentioned, saying that in the past ten years or so, domestic wars have been incessant. Most of the central administrative organs have been broken and incomplete in the event of war. The only one that has been able to maintain its integrity from beginning to end is the Customs. This is because all parties understand the integrity of customs administration and dare not lightly take great risks related to national economy and people's livelihood, not only because it is managed by foreigners. The customs revenue each year, in addition to offsetting foreign debts and indemnities, is used as a fund to guarantee domestic debts. These domestic debts are entirely in the hands of merchants and people, and the banking sector especially uses them as reserves. The total amount of debt is no less than 100 million yuan, which is the basis for the national economy. If the fund for domestic debts is affected by politics, the national finance and the people's economy will suffer a major blow. The government, merchants and people will all suffer. Therefore, in times of intense political strife, people are reluctant to destroy other organizations, but they can pay special attention to maintaining customs administration, because they fear that once destroyed, even if they are lucky enough to win and enter the central government, they will also be restricted by others and unable to stop them. Therefore, Yan Xishan of Shanxi, even if not for the sake of the national economy and people's livelihood, and China's foreign credit, should also consider his own future, and it is hoped that he will know the opportunity and retreat, and not rashly engage in it.

Today 124

Establishment of the Special District Citizens' Association

All Preparatory Committee Members Take Office

The Shanghai Special District Citizens' Association has been approved by the Municipal Party Department. It is scheduled to hold its inaugural meeting at 10:00 a.m. today (the 6th) in the auditorium of the Henan Road Merchants' Reorganization Association. All the preparatory committee members will be sworn in. The preparatory office has sent invitations to various party and government agencies and public organizations in advance to attend the ceremony. The inaugural hall has also been newly decorated by the preparatory committee members Xu Yunhui and others. The special district has a vast territory and a large population, and is the essence of the city. Taxpaying citizens should have a cohesive group with sufficient strength, so that there is hope for the progress of citizens' welfare. The Municipal Party Department, after several solemn studies, in order to unify the organization and expand its strength, resolutely ordered the dissolution of various classified organizations in the city (such as the Merchants' Association, etc.), and on the one hand, selected 39 citizens in the city who are knowledgeable, experienced and have a long-standing reputation in the community as members to be responsible for the preparation. The list of all preparatory committee members is recorded below:

Preparatory Committee Members: Qian Longzhang, Yu Hualong, Zhang Yichen, Cheng Xiechun, Xu Yunhui, Jiang Peizhao, Zheng Jiansan, Luo Qinghua, Zhang Henghai, Wu Liangsheng, Cheng Zhusheng, Hu Fengxiang, Chen Yiting, Yu Zhongxian, Wang Pingnan, Chen Weiwen, Zhang Zilian, Yu Mingxun, Xu Chenrong, Song Weiliang, Yan Esheng, Lu Qisheng, Cai Suizi, Dai Chunfeng (15 newly appointed members), Wang Zhaocheng, Wang Yansong, Yuan Ludeng, Tu Kaizheng, Cheng Guichu, Xi Guanglin, Chen Wenbin, Zhu Wenqi, Zhu Baoluo, Wu Zhihao,

Yu Yangsheng, Qiu Jiabiao, Chen Jicheng, Zhang Xianfang, Zheng Chengqing Inauguration Declaration China is unfortunate, defeated in the Opium War, resulting in unequal treaties, the so-called cession of land and indemnities, opening up of doors, tariff agreements, consular jurisdiction and other humiliating and humiliating rights, all began at that time. The imperialists of the world cited each other and competed to taste. In 1858, the renewal of the Sino-British trade treaty was the beginning of the concession. Since then, China has been in constant turmoil. Thieves and traitors have all used the concession as a refuge. This concession, which harbors dirt and accommodates filth, has become a haven for those who commit crimes. Gambling such as dog racing and roulette, kidnapping and robbery cases, the prevalence of opium, and the establishment of brothels have caused incalculable losses to the precious national currency. What I see and hear makes my heart ache. However, our two million citizens are content with temporary peace, forgetting the great shame of China, and are ignorant and unaware. They are bustling and noisy, like the deaf and dumb, willing to jump into the palms of their enemies, and lose the faces of Yan and Huang. Thinking of this, tears of blood fall. Alas, China is sinking, who can save the tide? I am born as a human being, how can I just feed like dogs and pigs? It is related to the country. The members of this association dare not follow the National Revolution and run around calling, awakening the people, standing together under the blue sky and white sun, and working hard for freedom and equality. Opening up the barriers and holding back the tide, valuing this nation that loves peace so much, and rounding up this earliest civilized China. Now, at the beginning of the establishment of this association, I use my sincerity to tell my dearest compatriots who are citizens in the Shanghai Concession, please trace the roots and rise up courageously, understand the mission of this association, supervise the progress of this association, unite as one, and work together. This is my declaration, and I ask for your public review.

Oath of Office We swear in utmost sincerity to accept the guidance of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department of the Chinese Kuomintang, to strive for the establishment of the Special District Citizens' Association, to seek the greatest interests of all citizens for freedom and equality, to seek the early realization of the recovery of the concession, and if we violate the oath, we are willing to accept the most severe punishment from the Chinese Kuomintang and all citizens. We swear.

Inauguration Notice After being commissioned by the Executive Committee of the Municipal Party Department, our committee members bear the mission of preparing for the establishment of the Special District Citizens' Association, and striving for the welfare of freedom and equality for all citizens. According to the outline promulgated by our Party Department, we will work hard to promote and achieve its duties. After the preparatory meeting, it was publicly decided to hold the inauguration ceremony of all the preparatory committee members at 10:00 a.m. on May 6th of the lunar calendar in the Tianhou Palace Bridge North Commercial Reorganization Association. In addition to submitting reports to the Party and government agencies to invite representatives to attend the swearing-in ceremony and inviting various agencies and organizations to send representatives to attend the ceremony, we will also publish a notice in the newspaper, respectfully hoping that representatives of various agencies and organizations will arrive on time and that all citizens of the city will freely participate in the ceremony and share the grand event.

Inauguration Order 1. The presidium takes its seats, all committee members take their seats, representatives of various organizations take their seats, and guests take their seats. 2. Play music. 3. Sing the Party song. 4. Pay the highest respect to the Party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of the Prime Minister. 5. The chairman reads the Prime Minister's will. 6. Silence. 7. 16. Photograph and dismiss the meeting.

Amended Articles of Association The Articles of Association of this Association have been amended and promulgated by the Municipal Party Department as follows: 1. This Association is named the Shanghai Special Municipality Special District Citizens' Association. 2. This Association is under the guidance and supervision of the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang, and handles preparatory matters in accordance with the Articles of Association of the Shanghai Special Municipality Special District Citizens' Association. 3. This Association has 31 to 45 members, who are appointed by the Municipal Party Department. 4. This Association has 5 to 9 standing committee members, who form the standing committee, and establishes general affairs, finance, guidance, registration, and investigation departments, each with a director. The standing committee members and the directors of each department are elected by the members of this Association. 5. Each department of this Association may employ staff members as appropriate according to the complexity of the affairs, and they are appointed with the approval of the meeting of this Association. 6. This Association holds a regular meeting once every two weeks, and the standing committee holds a meeting once a week. Meetings may be convened temporarily when necessary. The chairman is temporarily elected by the public. 7. The funds of this Association are raised by the meeting of this Association. 8. All regulations of this Association concerning preparatory matters and office procedures shall be submitted to the Municipal Party Department for approval and implementation. 9. The preparatory time of this Association is temporarily set at three months. 10. This Association will end immediately after the Shanghai Special Municipality Special District Citizens' Association is formally established. 11. The Articles of Association of this Association shall be promulgated and implemented by the Municipal Party Department.

Public Buses Partially Open Yesterday 129

Only Running on the Route Between Jing'an Temple and Waibaidu Bridge

The public bus strike has been going on for many days. Only the vehicles running on the route between Jing'an Temple and Waibaidu Bridge temporarily started running yesterday morning. There were a total of ten buses running on this route, all driven by Russians. The ticket sellers were Chinese. The windows around the bus were covered with silk screens. Each bus was seated with an armed patrolman. The fare was 30 copper coins regardless of distance. No incidents occurred yesterday.

Public Concession 130

Tram Strike News Yesterday

The Tram Strike Committee of the Public Concession held its seventh meeting on the afternoon of the 5th. First, dozens of striking committee members from the ten-member groups in various districts and the talks reported in detail on the situation of the workers. They unanimously agreed to adhere to the conditions to the end, and were especially resentful of the White Russians driving buses. Therefore, the following resolutions were unanimously passed: (1) The issues of all workers who drive, sell tickets, coppersmiths, turn on lights, pry roads, and pull lights must be resolved together. (2) A general meeting of all workers will be convened on the 8th. (3) Issue a written warning to a certain worker who is a traitor and a certain ticket seller. (4) Establish message reporting stations in various places. (5) Call on all workers to actively assist the striking bus brothers and deal severely with the White Russians. (6) If the employers send representatives to negotiate conditions with the strike committee, the superintendent must first sign a guarantee that the representatives will never be fired and that the representatives will be safe before representatives are sent to formally negotiate with the employers. It is absolutely forbidden to act as a representative privately. (7) Demand that the company dismiss a certain lawyer.

Great Competition in Sino-American Shipping 131

Osaka's Giant Ship Breaks and Loses Over One Million

The Pacific ship Alba, owned by the Japanese Osaka Company, a giant ship that travels the Sino-American line, with a load capacity of 10,000 net tons, sailing the Shanghai-Seattle route. Last time it came to Shanghai from the United States, it carried a large number of salted fish and other goods. When it traveled outside Yokohama Port, it encountered a strong wind and hit a reef. The hull was driven onto the reef. The company sent a ship to tow it. After more than a month of work, the ship was finally towed with cables. It was expected to pull it out in one fell swoop, but the front of the Alba was stuck in the reef and could not be pulled out. After the tugboat tried its best to pull it, the Alba broke into two pieces. The front half of the ship was still stuck on the rocks, and the rear half was towed into the sea, causing the ship to be completely sacrificed. Fortunately, the crew members were rescued first, so no one was injured. Of the goods loaded in Shanghai, a batch of salted fish could still be transferred, and other goods such as ink had completely melted into the sea. The ship was built after the European War and was the Osaka Company's largest and fastest ship, a sister ship to the Arimarenai Maru. This time, the accident caused a loss of more than one million yuan.

Kinei Maru Takes Over The company is building six high-speed giant ships to compete with British, American and Norwegian ships in Shanghai and New York on the Panama Canal to the Far East in order to compete for Sino-American transportation. Now, the company has changed its plan. Due to the accident of the Alba in the Pacific, it has decided to send the first of the six new ships, the Kinei Maru, to the Seattle route first. At the same time, because there are not many goods from China to the United States and our country's ship charter fee has been changed to the gold standard, the company has temporarily decided not to send the Pacific ship to Shanghai for five months to avoid tonnage tax. Now that the new ship has been completed, it has been decided to resume the Pacific route to Shanghai on July 1, and the Kinei Maru is scheduled to open its maiden voyage in mid-August.

New York Water Foot First Falls There are more than a dozen companies, including British Blue Funnel, Cheung Tai, Po Wo, Prince, Yih Tai, American Dollar, Balboa, and Norwegian Wheelock, that send ships on the Shanghai-New York route. During the previous silk rush in the Pacific, the export water foot on the New York line has also fallen. Now it is heard that Osaka will add six fast ships and will be able to open classes soon. British and American shipping companies, in order to maintain the equilibrium of their business in China and avoid being threatened by a major enemy, have decided to greatly reduce the import water foot from the United States to Shanghai before the Japanese ships are running. This is already being implemented. Generally, the freight for goods from the United States to Shanghai, which originally charged more than 6 jiao (a tenth of a yuan) of US dollars per hundred pounds of weight, has now been reduced to 3.5 to 4 jiao.

Japan Expands Trade with China 132

Increased Purchases of Coarse Grains for Shipment to Japan Japan needs food every day. It relies entirely on shipments from China for relief, so there are often unscrupulous merchants who smuggle rice and grains for export in our country. Since the strict prohibition of food rice exports, Japan has increased its purchase of coarse grains in China. From October last year to the end of last month, the amount of Chinese coarse grains shipped to Japan in this half year was more than in the previous half year. According to statistics, 77,000 tons of wheat flour were shipped, an increase of 22,000 tons compared with the previous period; 28,000 tons of rapeseed were shipped, an increase of 14,000 tons compared with the previous period; 10,000 tons of sesame were shipped, an increase of 5,000 tons compared with the previous period; 9,000 tons of beans were shipped, a decrease of 5,000 tons compared with the previous period, because a large batch of goods was shipped from Dalian; 2,000 tons of chicken eggs were shipped, a decrease of 5,000 tons compared with the previous period; 40,000 tons of bran were shipped; and 10,000 tons of ramie were shipped. From this month, the amount of coarse grains shipped to Japan will be even more than in the previous period. Japanese merchants expect that from now until the end of September, they will need to ship 20,000 tons of coarse grains to the Orient. Therefore, from the 2nd of this month, Shanghai has added two more ships with a tonnage of 4,000 tons each to transport this cargo. The Zhenghai Steamship Company in the Yangtze River has increased the number of ships sailing to eleven to load coarse grains and other goods.

Encouraging the Import of Yarn and Cloth to China China is the largest market for Japan's cotton yarn and foreign cloth exports. Shanghai, Hankou, Tianjin, Jiaozhou, Guangzhou, and Xiamen all have shipments. However, in the past three months, the number of Japanese piece goods and cotton yarn shipped to Shanghai has not been as prosperous as in the previous months. In order to reduce the cost of yarn and cloth and make it easier to promote sales, the Japanese have first reduced the water foot for printing cotton to Japan by one yuan per ton as a fundamental development plan. However, after the fee reduction was implemented, the first ship from Japan to Shanghai has arrived in Shanghai. The ship carried more than 1,400 pieces of yarn and cloth, but there was no significant development. Now Japanese merchants are planning to ask the ships on the Japanese-Shanghai line to also reduce the water foot for yarn and cloth as the first step to encourage the promotion of trade with China. At the same time, various merchants have organized a large-scale inspection team to go to various parts of China to investigate the development of Japanese goods. This time, the Kyushu Daily News of Fukuoka Nakajima Town has launched a visiting group to Shanghai. The members of the group are more than 50 people, all of whom are important figures in various businesses, who are responsible for the mission of promoting and investigating trade with China. They have arrived in Shanghai and are about to go to the Shanghai-Ningbo Road area to inspect.

Silk Cocoon Association Asks for Protection of the Cocoon Market 133

Huang Xiaochen, chairman of the Jiang, Zhejiang and Anhui Silk Cocoon General Association, believes that the new cocoons in the interior will be on the market soon. Silk cocoon merchants are carrying money to set off for the purchase of fresh cocoons. However, the various prefectures are not peaceful. Therefore, he is referring to the measures in previous years and has submitted documents to the National Government and the governments of the three provinces of Jiang, Zhejiang and Anhui, ordering them to strictly protect them to ensure the safety of farmers and merchants. The original document to the National Government is recorded below: It is submitted for the protection of the cocoon market, early preparations, and reference to the measures in previous years. It is respectfully requested that you examine and approve the distribution to the governments of the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang and Anhui to order their subordinate units with cocoons to strictly protect them to ensure the safety of farmers and merchants. It is imperative to investigate the cocoon markets in the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang and Anhui, which are troubled by different climates and different times. Most of them open markets in the middle of May in the lunar calendar, before and after the Xiaoman solar term. The cocoon shops all open markets one after another, with Zhejiang being the earliest. Over the years, the General Association has formulated measures, submitted them to the government, and distributed them to the governments of the three provinces for protection, and distributed the printed protection measures to the troops and county public security agencies in various places for investigation and handling, so that they can be carefully protected. I am extremely grateful for this year's cocoon market. To be prudent in light of the social situation and in the meticulous protection, Zhou Wenan's tranquility only exists where the waterways are divergent and far away from the county. Brigands are not yet settled and are all vigilant. Most of the areas in Jiang and Zhejiang are water transportation areas, and silver goods are exchanged. It is not enough to prevent troubles from happening unless capable troops are dispatched to patrol along the way. The banditry is more serious in northern Anhui and other places, and protection is especially important. The cocoon shops in various places are mostly located in rural towns, and the military and police forces are not as strong as those in cities. Farmers carry cocoons to the shops, and cocoon merchants carry silver to collect cocoons. The roads they pass must be maintained with real strength to eliminate the invisible troubles. The General Association is responsible for planning ahead and listing each item that should be protected, such as loading and transporting cash and transporting cocoon packages, with reference to the past situation over the years, and respectfully asking the government to preside over the handling and approve the distribution to the governments of Jiangsu, Zhejiang and Anhui three months in advance, and quickly order the troops stationed in each place with cocoons and the county government to protect the army, the government, the water and land public security in accordance with the rules, and the General Association shall print multiple copies of the articles and methods, divide them into 100 copies per province, and present them to the three provincial governments for distribution to the county governments and military and police officers in charge of cocoon protection for investigation and handling. The reason for the early request for protection of the cocoon scarf is attached and the methods are submitted for your examination and record, and please order them to be followed, which is for the public convenience (the documents submitted to the three provinces of Jiang, Zhejiang and Anhui are roughly the same and omitted)

Local News Two

Fire Outside Datongmen 135

Six Lives Burned to Death

The Woman Was Exhausted After Childbirth

Pulling Her Children and Calling Her Daughters, She Could Not Take Care of Everything

When She Woke Them Up One by One to Escape

The Smoke Was Thick and There Was No Way Out

The lower floor of Dexing Cai's laundry and dyeing shop at No. 207 Huayuan Lane, outside Datongmen in the southern city, was rented to people who worked as bamboo weavers. At 3:00 a.m. yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out, and it spread rapidly, breaking through the roof and spreading to Huaxing firewood shop at No. 205 and Wanhe longan shop at No. 201. Fire trucks from various fire brigades drove to the scene to put out the fire, but the fire was fierce. The houses at these three addresses were all three-courtyard deep, and a total of nine houses were reduced to ashes. They were extinguished in time and did not spread. However, because it was late at night when the fire broke out, everyone was asleep. Although adults who were physically active all escaped the smoke and fire, Zhang Changbao, a tenant of the Huaxing firewood shop at No. 205, was from Jiangbei and worked as a foreman on the Dahua轮船 that ran on the Yangtze River. He had just set sail the day before yesterday and left his wife Zhang Guo (38 years old), daughter Daya (15 years old), son Pangzai (13 years old), son Dengsanzi (10 years old), son Xiaosanzi (8 years old), and son Maotou (half a month old) at home. She had not been out of confinement for long and was mentally exhausted. When she saw the fire, she woke up in shock, pulling her children and calling her daughters. Because there were so many children, she could not take care of everything. When she woke them up one by one to put on their clothes and escape, the fire had reached them and the smoke blocked the way. She was physically weak after childbirth and had no courage to break through the fire. She was worried about the children and could not go, so she pulled them together and was burned to death miserably. Yesterday morning, six bodies of all sizes were dug out, all with scorched heads, swollen bellies, and burst open. The scene was so tragic that it made people feel sad. The police station in District 1 is investigating and arresting the arsonist. In addition, it ordered the land chief Lu Rongde of the 16th shop to report to the local court for investigation. In the afternoon, at 4 o'clock, Prosecutor Liu and Inspector Xuan came to the scene to investigate and confirmed that they had been burned to death. The sub-landlord Wu Jucai complained about the previous situation, and said that her husband had not yet been informed. The prosecutor ordered her to collect the bodies on his behalf and wait for the arsonist to be brought to justice.

Undercover Detectives Misunderstand and Shoot 136

One Undercover Detective Died

The Pedestrian Killed Was Xu Renjie

The Two Bodies Were Autopsied Together Yesterday Morning

The Police Station Gave Compensation to Both of Them

Four People Were Injured and Their Injuries Were Very Serious

The Xinzha Police Station has recently had cases of midnight robbery in its jurisdiction, especially in the Changsha Road and Guling Road area. Therefore, it dispatches patrolmen and undercover patrolmen to patrol every midnight. Unexpectedly, the detectives met on Changsha Road around half past midnight the day before yesterday, misunderstood each other, and shot each other, resulting in a tragedy. Three Chinese detectives and two undercover detectives were shot and injured. One of the undercover detectives died, and a pedestrian was killed by a stray bullet. The details have been recorded in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that the person killed by the stray bullet was named Xu Renjie. Afterwards, the police station ordered the body to be taken to the Forensic Examination Office on Fieling Road together with the body of Chinese police officer Liu Shangwu, an undercover detective of No. 392. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Xu, commissioned by the Local Court of the Special District, came to the office to examine the body, ascended to his official position, and inquired about the situation at the time. According to Xu's father, Xu Shida, the deceased was his son, 23 years old, and worked in the stock exchange. He went out to buy things that day and died in an accident. According to Liu Wang, the wife of Liu, she is 32 years old, from Tianjin, and now lives at No. 118 Kang Nuot Road. My husband died in the line of duty, and I request preferential treatment. The head of the Xinzha Police Station reported that although the police officer died due to a misunderstanding, his loyalty to his duties has been demonstrated, and the Municipal Council should give preferential treatment in accordance with the regulations. As for the death of Xu Renjie, appropriate compensation should also be given. Prosecutor Xu then ordered Xu Shida and Liu Wang to execute a bond separately to receive the body for coffin burial, and ordered the police station to give compensation. However, the remaining three Chinese detectives and one undercover detective are still being treated in the hospital, and their injuries are serious, and they have not yet been out of danger.

Zhang San Accuses 137

Concubine Intends Poisoning

A bowl of poisonous congee as evidence, and a small bottle also highly suspicious. Zhang San, a native of Haizhou, yesterday filed a complaint with the Fifth District Third Precinct against his concubine, Zhang Zhao, stating that he lived at No. 19 Linping Road, Hujia Muqiao, and had been in a cohabiting relationship with the woman for four years. Now, because she has fallen in love with someone else, her heart has changed. On February 1st of this year, she secretly put medicine into the congee, intending to poison me to death. I took a bite and found it very bitter, so I quickly spat it out and asked her to taste it. Unexpectedly, she refused to eat it and said there was poison in it. I thought that since she hadn't tasted it, how could she know there was poison, which was clearly a plot to harm me. At the time, I intended to seize her, but my mother persuaded me, saying that since I hadn't seen her putting the poison in, I couldn't be sure. So I kept the congee in an iron basin. (He then presented the congee.) But afterwards, I just let it slide and didn't pursue the matter. Unexpectedly, when I woke up yesterday morning, a small bottle suddenly fell to the ground during an argument. I wanted to pick it up and look at it, but she quickly grabbed it and hid it, refusing to show it to anyone. I immediately questioned her, but she escaped. I suspect she is plotting something again, putting poison to harm me. So today, I found her and brought the case to you, asking for an investigation, etc. When questioned, she claimed to be 31 years old and denied any intention to harm, saying she was fleeing due to being abused, etc. The precinct, believing the case involved attempted murder, transferred both parties to the District Court for preliminary examination by the prosecutor, who ordered the congee to be tested for poisonous substances before further investigation.

Hangzhou Silk Selling Well in Southeast Asia 139

Shanghai Market Shortage and High Prices

Currently, this group has received telegrams from Singapore and other places, wanting to purchase several thousand bolts of Hangzhou silk. Therefore, the market price has risen from 6 jiao to 6 jiao 3 or 4. The stock of Hangzhou goods in Shanghai is weak, and if the demand is urgent, prices may rise further.

Monstrous Birth: A Tumor, Not a Head 144

Yesterday morning around 8:00 AM, there was a sudden rumor in Caojiadu Town, Western Shanghai, that a woman surnamed Mou in the Xinchang Workshop had given birth to a two-headed child.

As a result, everyone echoed the rumor, causing a sensation throughout the town. People rushed to see it, all amazed and shocked. However, the family considered it a disgrace and kept the doors tightly closed, preventing outsiders from seeing it. Thus, the rumor spread even more wildly. A reporter heard about it and went to the site around 2:00 PM to investigate. It was at the home of Shen Ruming, No. 48 Xinchang Workshop, behind the Western Post Office at the Triangular Ground in the town. The mother, surnamed Zhu, was Shen's sister-in-law, 24 years old, from Jiangyin. She had arrived in Shanghai from her hometown the day before yesterday and was staying at Shen's place. The woman had been pregnant for twelve months, and her belly was unusually large, which people found strange. The day before yesterday, after arriving in Shanghai, Shen's wife took her to tour the various workshops in the factory for half a day. She went to bed that evening and did not feel any abdominal pain. But after getting up yesterday morning, she suddenly felt excruciating stomach pains and immediately called for a midwife. When the child was born, the midwife was shocked to see something resembling a head hanging between the child's legs. The child had already died. So she put it in a wooden basin and abandoned it outside the door for public viewing. The reporter saw that the child was female, with fully formed limbs and features. Between her legs was a tumor, about the size of a soccer ball, about five or six inches in diameter, attached to the body with a base only an inch or so thick. After someone picked it up, the tumor hung down like a large ball, about twice the size of her head. Bloodstains were visible in the basin. Viewers called it a miracle. In fact, it was not two heads but a monstrous birth. Until evening, people continued to come to see it.

Hu Guofan Attempts Suicide in the New Tibet Hotel 145

Reason Unknown

Life is in Great Danger

Hu Guofan, claiming to be twenty-eight years old and a native of Shaoxing, wearing a yellow serge jacket and black silk vest, arrived at the New Tibet Hotel, No. 335 Tibet Road, behind the New World, on the 29th of last month. He opened Room 25 on the upper floor of the hotel and paid three yuan. For several days, he behaved normally. Unexpectedly, yesterday at noon, the tea server asked Hu Guofan for the room bill, as it was overdue. Hu replied that he would pay everything off at 6:00 PM. The servants, as he was a regular customer, did not pay much attention. When it was past 6:00 PM, the tea server knocked on the door, as Hu was still asleep. There was no answer. The servants knew something was wrong and forced the door open. They found Hu barely breathing, on the verge of death. They immediately reported it to the Xinzha Police Station, which dispatched Chinese Constable 196 and Western Constable 265 to investigate. They observed that Hu's face was pale and white foam was coming from the corners of his mouth, indicating poisoning. They did not find a suicide note on his person. Later, they found two empty bottles of sedative pills in the drawer of the table. The constables sent Hu to Renji Hospital for treatment. According to the doctor, his condition was critical and his life was in danger.

Hu Yicheng Cries Wildly in a Rickshaw 146

Failed Attempted Abduction of Wang Dabao

Hu Yicheng, a native of Yancheng, living in the Yutong West Thatched Cottage in Zhabei, makes a living pulling a rickshaw. Last spring, through matchmakers Jin Liu and Jin Jiang, he engaged Wang Dabao, a woman of the same origin, as his wife. Hu, having lost both parents and being advanced in years, urgently wanted to start a family. So last winter, he asked the matchmakers to choose a date for the wedding. Unexpectedly, at that time, Dabao's mother suddenly said that her daughter was only sixteen and had not yet developed, so it would have to be postponed for several years. Hu was very angry after learning this, because although Dabao was young, she was tall and robust, looking over twenty years old. So he secretly suspected that there must be a change, but he did not dare to be dogmatic. The day before yesterday, he again asked the original matchmakers to speak, but Dabao's stepfather, Shang San, came out to obstruct, seemingly wanting to break the engagement. Hu was very afraid. Yesterday, he went with the matchmakers and others. When Shang was not home, they carried Dabao out and forced her into a rickshaw, driving away quickly. Unexpectedly, Dabao cried wildly along the way. A police officer on duty, seeing this, was surprised and stopped them, asking for the reason. He arrested Hu and the others and took them to the Fourth District Headquarters. Chief Jin questioned Hu, who said, "In the past, I hired Liu and Jiang as matchmakers to introduce Dabao to me as my wife, and I paid a dowry of 90 yuan. Her mother agreed to it in one go. At that time, her mother was widowed and had not yet cohabited with anyone. She urged me to complete the marriage as soon as possible. Unexpectedly, now she has repeatedly procrastinated, because her lover is instigating from the middle and does not want to live a proper life." The matchmakers also testified that they were indeed the ones who brokered the deal, but they did not know why a dispute had suddenly arisen between the two parties. The judge ordered Dabao's parents to be brought in for further questioning.

A Barber of Utmost Shamelessness 147

Enters Someone's Home at Night

What Does He Do in Bed?

Yesterday morning around 3:00 AM, there was a sound of fighting and shouting inside No. 51 Hengfeng Road, Zhabei. A police officer on duty at the Fourth District station nearby went to investigate, knocking on the door and entering. He saw two men and one woman wrestling together and immediately arrested them all. According to Gu Bentao, "My wife, Li, is usually well-behaved, and our relationship is strong. Unexpectedly, recently a barber named Gui Wenqing, seeing her beauty, became lustful and made advances to my wife, which she rejected. Tonight, he sneaked into my house, hid in my wife's room, and when she was asleep, jumped into bed and groped her, intending to rape her. Fortunately, I returned home and wanted to take Gui to the police station. Just then, the police officer arrived, please investigate." Li testified, "I am 22 years old. I was just in a dream when suddenly a man came to sleep with me." Gui Wenqing testified, "The day before yesterday, Li asked me to cut her hair and strongly urged me to have an affair with her. Because I could not refuse, I went to meet her tonight. Li did not refuse. Unexpectedly, her husband returned home and falsely accused me of rape." The judge ordered an investigation and interrogation.

Handwriting of the Bandit 148

Is the Same as the Extortionist Bandit

Five Letters in Total, the Last One Very Serious

Owner of a Foreign Cloth Store Reports to the Police for Investigation

Zhou Xingbin, owner of Zhou Fuji Foreign Cloth Store at No. 558 Jiujiang Road, received a threatening letter on the 21st of last month, demanding 5,000 yuan. He initially ignored it. Letters continued to arrive, five in total. The last letter, on the 2nd of this month, was extremely harsh, saying that if he did not agree, they would use some means to deal with him, and that the location for negotiation would be notified separately. The next day, Zhou received a phone call from the bandit, instructing him to go to the entrance of the Qianjiang Guild Hall at the corner of Peng Road and North Henan Road at 2:00 PM that afternoon, holding a bundle of newspapers as a sign. Zhou reported it to the Old Gate Police Station, which dispatched Detectives Liu Junqing and Song Bingzheng, and Investigator Pang Yutang, who went to the appointed location that afternoon. At 2:40 PM, Zhang Jinxian from Suzhou was seen loitering there and was captured by the detectives and taken to the police station. He was ordered to write numbers, which were compared with the letters received by Zhou. The handwriting was found to be the same. So yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Special District Court, where Judge Zhou conducted a preliminary hearing and then ordered him to be detained, postponing the investigation of his accomplices.

Arrest and Imprisonment of Pudian Bandits 153

An elderly woman from Pudian, Cai Xu, came to Shanghai from her hometown the day before yesterday. She took a ferry to the Huangpu Bund Wharf in the French Concession. Just as she landed, she was suddenly attacked by bandits Li Fuggen and Xu Afu, who worked together to forcibly pull off a pair of gold earrings she was wearing, causing her ears to bleed profusely. She reported to the police station, and Chief immediately sent Detectives Lu Jinchen and Bao Tamer Jiang Changwen to arrest Li and Xu. They found the stolen goods and took them to the police station. Yesterday, they were escorted to the French Court for investigation. First, Western Detective (unclear name) went to the court and reported the situation, stating that the defendants were found to be specializing in robbing the gold ornaments and luggage of Pudong villagers and travelers at the dock, which was extremely illegal and violated Article 343 of the Criminal Law, requesting severe punishment. Then, the plaintiff recounted the circumstances of the robbery. Li Fuggen and Xu Afu admitted to colluding to rob the ornaments. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Li to 18 months in the Western Prison and Xu to one year to serve as a warning.

Photo Telegraph 158

To Switch to Wireless Transmission

Effective June 1st

The photo telegraph service, established by the Ministry of Communications, originally used the Beijing-Shanghai long-distance telephone lines for transmission. However, due to frequent disruptions and line damage, the Ministry of Communications has decided to switch to wireless transmission. It is said that the plan is largely complete and will be implemented on June 1st. In the future, it will be extended to major ports. All major ports in the interior with wireless stations will be able to send and receive photo telegrams.

Anhui Province Uses Shanghai Rice to Aid Famine Victims 160

The rice-producing areas of Anhui Province are now experiencing famine, leading to a shortage of food for the people. Famine victims are rushing to buy rice, and in Anqing, this has led to rice shops closing. The Anhui Provincial Government has decided to implement price controls to help the famine victims, reducing the price of rice by five yuan per shi (unit of measure). It has also issued an order prohibiting rice from leaving the province. However, because there is not much rice stored in Anqing and Wuhu, it is stipulated that each person can only buy five sheng (unit of measure) of rice per day. After famine victims purchase the rice, the police force them to soak it in water before taking it away to prevent unscrupulous people from buying and reselling it. Fearing that there will not be enough rice for everyone, the provincial committee has decided to send a rice purchasing committee led by Jin Teng to Shanghai to purchase 10,000 shi of foreign rice for the implementation of price controls. Yesterday, the provincial government also sent a telegram to China Merchants and Sanbei shipping companies, asking them to transport the rice for free to facilitate famine relief. Yesterday, the shipping companies agreed to reduce the shipping costs of the rice, and the first batch of rice purchased in Shanghai, over 1,000 shi, was shipped yesterday.

Jisheng Association 161

The Latest Situation of the Shaanxi Disaster Received

The Chinese Jisheng Association in this city recently received an urgent telegram from Yan Lin and others of the Qishan County Disaster Relief Branch in Shaanxi, stating that Qishan has unfortunately suffered from continuous droughts for years, compounded by repeated wars. There has been no rain for three years and no harvest for four years. A personal inspection of the disaster situation in various villages reveals that over 63,700 people have died of starvation and over 16,400 households have fled to other provinces. The county's population has decreased by nearly two-thirds, leading to barren fields and vacant houses, with seven or eight out of ten houses empty. Corpses are piled up, people and animals are eating each other, and people are selling their wives and children, facing separation and death. They earnestly request the rapid provision of disaster relief funds to save the remaining people. They express deep gratitude for the assistance provided, and the urgent tone of the telegram is overwhelming. The disaster situation in Qishan County is so dire that the situation in other counties can be imagined. The association distributed emergency relief and seeds in Qishan last year. The dire situation was personally witnessed and reported by the association's personnel. The spring famine is worsening day by day, and there is no way to help or do anything. The association's Shaanxi Disaster Relief Director Zhang Junxianqing set off on April 22nd to provide relief in Shaanxi, hoping to avert the disaster.

Central Bank Inspection Report 162

52nd Time

The 52nd Central Bank Issuance Reserve Inspection Report states that, in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, the association is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the issuance of convertible notes by the bank. The 52nd inspection was conducted on April 30, 1920, at the bank's issuing bureau. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: Total amount of convertible notes issued: 14,351,883 silver dollars, including 13,175,290 silver dollar notes and 1,176,593 auxiliary currency notes. Total amount of convertible note reserves: 14,351,883 silver dollars, including 9,448,878.2 silver dollars in cash reserves, of which 5,600,788.31 silver dollars are stored in the bank's issuing vault, 1,331,035.14 silver dollars are in branch banks in various ports, and 2,500,964.75 silver dollars are deposited with other banks. Guarantee reserves: equivalent to 4,903,004.8 silver dollars. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve should be 60% and the guarantee reserve should be 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guarantee reserve does not exceed 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby submitted. April 30, 1920, Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun, Supervisors Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Zou Xiangqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiyu.

Radio Operator Licenses for Ships' Radio Stations 171

Provisional Regulations Promulgated

The Radio Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications has officially promulgated the Provisional Regulations for the Issuance of Radio Operator Licenses for Ships' Radio Stations. The regulations are disclosed below: Article 1: All radio personnel on ships (referring to Chinese ships and foreign ships navigating along the coast of China and inland areas) must hold a radio operator license for ships' radio stations (hereinafter referred to as radio operator license) issued by the Radio Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications (hereinafter referred to as the Radio Administration Bureau) to perform their duties. Article 2: Radio operator licenses are divided into first and second classes. Applicants for licenses must pass the examination conducted by the Radio Administration Bureau, register with the Ministry, and be issued licenses according to their class. Article 3: The examination for issuing radio operator licenses will be held once every quarter. The date and location will be designated and notified by the Radio Administration Bureau. Article 4: Any person who is in good health, over sixteen years of age, has completed the internship period in a ship or coastal radio station, possesses the knowledge and skills specified in Articles 5, Paragraphs 1 and 2, and has a certificate issued by the person in charge of the service radio station may apply to the Radio Administration Bureau for examination, and pay an application fee of one yuan, and two recent two-and-a-half-inch head-and-shoulder photos. This application fee and photos will not be returned regardless of whether the applicant passes the examination or not. Article 5: Applicants must possess the following knowledge and skills: 1. First-class radio operator (1) Party Ideology Wisdom (2) Clear and fluent Chinese (3) Ability to write essays in English (4) Essentials of the World Radiocommunication Convention, Communication Rules, Calling Methods, and Radio Telegraph Abbreviations (5) Essentials of Electricity, Principles of Radio Telegraphy, Mobile Stations, Transmitters and Receivers, Generators, Storage Batteries, and other theoretical and experimental applications, common knowledge, and skills to repair the aforementioned machines (6) Ability to transmit and receive the internationally used Morse code at an average speed of 20 groups per minute accurately (each group consists of five letters, numbers, or symbols). 2. Second-class radio operator (1) Basic knowledge of Party Ideology (2) Clear and fluent Chinese (3) Ability to write short English passages (4) Various rules regarding radio communication (5) Elementary principles of electricity and radio telegraphy, mobile stations, transmitters and receivers, generators, storage batteries, and simple common knowledge for using and maintaining the aforementioned machines (6) Ability to transmit and receive the internationally used Morse code at an average speed of 16 groups per minute accurately (each group consists of five letters, numbers, or symbols). Article 6: The examination subjects are divided into Party Ideology, Chinese, English, Electrical Law (radio law and wired electricity applicable to radio), Radio Science, and Transmission and Reception, six subjects in total. Except for Radio Science and Transmission and Reception, which must have a score of 80 or higher, a total score of 250 or higher in the other subjects is considered passing. Article 7: Holders of a second-class radio operator license must wait at least three years before applying for the first-class radio operator license upgrade examination. Article 8: When obtaining a license, a license fee of three yuan and a stamp tax of one yuan must be paid. Article 9: The validity period of each radio operator license is as follows: (1) Those who apply before the end of June each year will expire at the end of December of the following year. (2) Those who apply before the end of December each year will expire at the end of June of the third year. Article 10: If you want to continue to apply for a license when the license expires, you should request a new license three months before the expiration date and pay the fee as stipulated in Article 8. However, if you have changed to another job for more than half a year in the middle, you should retake the exam when applying for a new license. Article 11: If the license is lost, it should be declared in the newspaper, and the fee should be paid as stipulated in Article 8 to request a replacement. Article 12: Those who have passed the examination of the former Radio Administration Office of the Ministry of Communications and have obtained a license may bring their old license and a certificate from the person in charge of the ship's radio station where they are currently working to the Bureau within two months after the promulgation of these regulations to exchange for a new license, and pay the fee as stipulated in Article 8. After two months, the aforementioned old licenses will be invalid. Article 13: If a ship's radio operator has any of the following circumstances, the Radio Administration Bureau may revoke his license or declare it invalid in the newspaper: (1) Violating the International Radiocommunication Convention and its attached business rules, or the telecommunications regulations promulgated by the Ministry of Communications and various regulations, and laws and regulations related to radio, and the Radio Administration Bureau deems it necessary to revoke the license or declare it invalid after review. (2) Disclosing the secrets of communication. (3) Using telecommunications to obstruct public business. (4) Failing to perform duties when a ship is in danger. (5) Receiving criminal punishment. (6) Bad conduct, which has been reported and investigated by superiors and found to be true. (7) Other circumstances not listed but similar to the above. Article 14: Radio operators whose licenses have been revoked or declared invalid by the Radio Administration Bureau shall not apply for re-examination. Article 15: If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, they may be submitted to the Ministry for amendment at any time. Article 16: These regulations will take effect from the date of promulgation. The temporary licenses issued by the Bureau before it holds the examination will remain valid.
