Special Feature

Xu Peikun's Proposal to Remedy the Low Silver Price and High Gold Price 174

Since the international gold price soared, the financial community in our country has been in extreme panic. The Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce have been trying to remedy the situation, but no effective method has yet been found. Now, economist Xu Peikun has expressed his opinion on the remedy. Mr. Xu is a professor at the School of Commerce of Central University and has a deep understanding of economic issues. We are publishing his opinion below:

In recent times, the sharp drop in silver exchange rates in Shanghai has deeply affected the people of our country, second only to the recurrence of civil war. The sharp drop in silver exchange rates has greatly affected the business community, but ordinary consumers and innocent people have also suffered significant sacrifices. The disaster has spread, and innocent bystanders can hardly escape. Furthermore, China's economic structure will be destroyed as a result. If not, it will only be given a glimmer of hope for recovery, allowing it to linger on. At this critical juncture, domestic bankers, economists, journalists, government officials, and all those who are concerned about current affairs are unanimously investigating the truth of this trend, repeatedly discussing it, and jointly seeking ways to save it. After careful observation of the occurrence of this trend, I have always advocated that the sharp drop in silver exchange rates is half due to the chaos in our country's currency system and half due to the illegal manipulation of the gold exchange (please refer to page 29 of the Commercial Magazine, January 25). Therefore, the way to save it is to prohibit the import of silver and at the same time prohibit speculative trading in gold. On the other hand, the protection of the silver price in our country is actually a necessity. The interests of domestic holders of large amounts of silver and other assets valued in silver cannot be unprotected due to the sharp drop in silver prices. As for the gold standard issue, the author knows that China is not ready to adopt it in the next few years. Even if China has adopted the gold standard system, our country will still have the problem of excessive fluctuations in exchange rates in the next few years, which must be dealt with. At the same time, it is necessary to find ways to maintain the value of large amounts of silver in the country. Therefore, the gold standard policy is not a good way to save the current trend, and besides, the gold standard proposal itself is a problem. Since the author published the above opinion, many economists and bankers have risen up and jointly suggested a ban on the import of silver or other import restrictions. Although there have been criticisms afterwards, they are mostly unsubstantial and have absolutely no reasoned arguments, so there is no need to correct them. In this article, the author will further elaborate on his previous opinions, hoping to dispel biased and unfounded discussions.

(B) Origin of the Misconception Regarding the High Price of Gold and the Low Price of Silver

In this unprecedented dramatic change in China's financial history, many scholars have been confused by it, resulting in confusion and misunderstandings. Some even say that the silver price is a global phenomenon, and the way to save it must be jointly agreed upon by the countries involved to seek a solution. To make their argument more forceful, they cite the law of supply and demand as proof, saying that the production of silver has increased rapidly in recent years, while the demand for silver has decreased significantly because India and Annam have successively adopted the gold standard. Another group argues that the parity of the Shanghai silver exchange rate is often based on the London silver price, and its calculation method is as follows: "Suppose today's London spot silver is one shilling and ten pence, then theoretically the parity of Shanghai is 22X1.175‖25.85d." Therefore, this group says that the Chinese silver price is determined by the London spot silver price, and China cannot control the silver price.

The Impact of Gold Speculation The above statements are nothing more than evasions. According to them, China itself has no way to remedy this trend. If so, what is the difference between resigning to fate? If we think about the above statement a little, we can know that the reason for this error is entirely because they have failed to recognize the real cause of this sharp drop in silver exchange rates, which has led to it. What is surprising is that many scholars have been misled by an erroneous starting point, and then submerged in an empty ideal, and do not know that the key to this problem lies in the expansion and contraction of gold speculation prices. Because of the expansion and contraction of gold speculation prices, the Shanghai silver exchange rate has undergone dramatic changes. In order to understand the truth of this problem, we must first truly recognize that this trend is purely an exchange rate trend, which is closely related to the rise and fall of gold speculation in Shanghai. (1) The Applicability of the Law of Supply and Demand First, we must know that the law of supply and demand cannot be abused. Before citing the law, we must first investigate the nature of a problem and the class system of its applicable principles. From this point of view, we know that the law of supply and demand is not universally applicable. When the demand for something increases, its price does not necessarily increase with it. Sometimes it still remains at the original price or even falls. This is very obvious, because under the condition of mass production, the production cost per unit of goods is often reduced as a result. Conversely, when the demand for something decreases, its price may not decrease with the decrease in demand due to the increase in production costs or the occurrence of other sacrifices. Furthermore, from the supply side, we can also explain that the scarcity of goods cannot immediately increase prices. Because when the price of something is too high, everyone can buy other things to replace it. And those that are scarce may be those that are half unsuitable for the times. Because they are half unsuitable for the times, their selling price can only be low, in order to compensate for part of the loss of effectiveness. Furthermore, when the supply of something is too abundant, its price does not necessarily decrease immediately, because although there are many, it can be reprocessed into other consumer goods, or temporarily stored, to wait for use in different times and places. What is said above is the limitation of the law of supply and demand. Those who talk about principles must not fail to observe, and must not fail to know that what is applied when talking about price fluctuations is a price principle, not just a law of supply and demand. (To be continued)

Plan to Protect Wartime Cultural Products 180

Initiated by French Intellectuals

Requesting Support from European Countries

Paris News: The Liangyou Association, affiliated with the French Lorry Museum, has now launched a movement to use a "cultural flag" to protect all scientific institutions, art academies, museums, historical monuments, etc. during wartime, so as to prevent them from being destroyed by war. Dr. Kickerford, an international law scholar at the University of Paris, has drafted a treaty on the use of the cultural flag. France is rich in art and antiquities, and public opinion generally supports this plan. It is generally believed that the Louvre Museum in Paris contains thousands of ancient paintings and treasures. If this treaty is concluded, this museum can also be preserved even if Paris falls to the enemy in future wars. Professor Lowry, who initiated the movement, said, "The cornerstone of future culture is based on beauty and knowledge. Therefore, the artistic treasures created by the ancients must be cherished and passed on to future generations. This must be the responsibility of all countries together. In short, cultural products belong to the whole world and are not the private property of any one country." The initiators are currently seeking support for this plan from European countries.

Dutch Female Writer

Ann McGruder's New Book

Woman's Cross Chang

Society is evolving day by day, and the women who are imprisoned in the male-centered social prison are gradually rebelling due to the hints of the times. They want to fight for and enjoy everything that men and women should enjoy, such as love, marriage, freedom, happiness, and sexuality. Therefore, in recent decades, the works of female writers have mostly focused on love and marriage. This is an expression of resistance to the old era and a genuine demand for women to be treated as individuals. In the countries near the Scandinavian Peninsula, the climate is cold, and thoughts tend to be dull. The remaining poison of the old religion makes it even more difficult for women's thoughts to develop. Therefore, in recent decades, only two female writers, Andassi and Ravloqui, have emerged in literature, and only Ellen Key has been able to fight for women's rights. However, in recent years, the neighboring Netherlands has also been stirred by the German women's struggle for suffrage after the war, and rebellious people have emerged among women. Ann McGruder's work is the most profound in clearly writing out her rebellious thoughts as propaganda.

The lady's first work, "The Rebellious Generation" (Th. Rebel Generation), profoundly and objectively writes out the bitterness and concepts of modern people. It is merely a naturalistic description. However, in the past fifteen years, many men, especially women, have found their own forms in her works. After this work, she went through a period of silence until 1925, when she wrote the sequel to this work, "Tantalus," which more profoundly wrote out the sorrow and despair of wives, carving out a mirror for women to reflect themselves. When this work was published in 1925, she immediately received wide praise, especially the description of women's fight to gain civil rights, which gave women great excitement. Now she has written the third sequel. In this "Woman's Crusade" (womensCtusade), Mrs. Pankhurst is her important protagonist, and the entire description focuses on women's political activities and struggles. This work is more powerful and tighter than the previous two episodes in depicting the active struggle of women to fight for freedom, happiness, and political equality. It can represent her recent mature thoughts. This second sequel has not yet been published. Recently, she gave a lecture in Basel and read several tense chapters from it to the audience. Her long trilogy is more meaningful than the historical novels of the Middle Ages by the Norwegian female writer Andassi. Her future is bound to be a race between the goddess of freedom and Ellen Key in the Scandinavian Peninsula. We are looking forward to the arrival of the "Woman's Cross" (Changxi).

Social News Submission Guidelines

(1) Articles are limited to news about science, industry, commerce, rural areas, health, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life at home and abroad.

(2) Pictures are limited to various lyrical paintings about social life.

(3) Photographs of seasonal scenery, flora and fauna, people, and newsworthy events are acceptable. Seasonal landscape photography with beautiful women is especially welcome.

(4) Each article should not exceed 2,000 words.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write the manuscript horizontally, and do not write illegibly. Western characters can be omitted where possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw pictures, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black ink.

(8) Please indicate that the submission is for the Social News Department.

Art Circle

Modern Danish Literature 181

Zhao Jingshen lectures at Fudan University

Tang Zengxie and Chen Xie take notes

My topic was originally "Modern Scandinavian Literature," which includes the writings of Denmark, Norway, and Sweden. That scope is relatively large. Now, due to time constraints, I will only talk about Danish literature first. I can continue to talk about the rest when I have the opportunity.

The "Modern Danish Literature" that I am talking about is from 1900 to the present (tgoooydeent). Chinese people have never paid much attention to Danish literature, and it is rarely mentioned. The most familiar are only three people. One is Hans Christian Andersen (HCAnptesen), a world-famous fairy tale writer. Another is Georg Brandes (G. raude, s), a famous critic. In addition, there is also the author of "Two Legs" and "Twelve Sisters," "Ewaed," who has single-volume translations in Chinese. We have translations by Mr. Li Xiaofeng and Mr. Yuan Jiahua. Regarding Danish literature, apart from these three people, others seem to be very unfamiliar. What I want to talk to you about now is 20th-century Danish literature, not 19th-century Danish literature.

Danish literature had great achievements in the 19th century. For example, Brandes not only gave the Danish people great glory, but also had a great influence on Norway, Sweden, and other countries around the world. As for modern Danish literature, it is often the new trend of international thought. It has a very important position in the Scandinavian Peninsula and is a channel for importing new trends.

Danish literature can be divided into three aspects:

(A) Novels

In the field of Danish novels, a large group of people emerged. They are all from Jutland (jutlahd), so they are called the Jutland School (Jutlandess). Their literary movement is called the Jutland Movement (JutandMouement).

Because Jutland is in the north of the world, facing the sea on three sides, the weather is very cold, and the people's occupations are mostly farming and fishing. They are very capable of developing the local nature and describing the local customs in detail, so the atmosphere of Soilofsoil is very strong in their works.

Johannes V. Jensen (I873), born in 1873, his father studied veterinary medicine, his grandfather was a weaver, and his ancestors were farmers. Therefore, Jensen's works and outlook on life cannot escape from objects such as local conditions and nature. In 1896, he wrote a book "The Danes", and in 1898, "EmerElkar". His work was most influenced by Jobannes Ioroensen. After traveling to the Americas between 1904 and 1905, he wrote several novels. He began to accept foreign influences. His works are novel in thought, extremely vivid, and the themes are mostly past and present, and the objects of life and nature. The work is full of humor and sadness. Later, he wrote many books, and his thoughts gradually stabilized. The main element of Jensen's thought is to promote the spirit of his Gothic race. At the same time, he strongly believes in Darwin's theory of evolution in science. Some say that Jensen's theory of evolution is a literary theory of evolution and has no life. Regarding the theory of evolution, he wrote "Evolution and Morality" in 1925 and "Animal Metamorphosis" in 1927. Although the description is inevitably absurd and empty, it can be regarded as his own expression of a "theory of evolution". Jensen wrote "The King's Failure" between 1900 and 1901. The protagonist of the book is the Danish king Clouskian II's political failure. Writing about America has 奥拉D、ork "Madam" "East Wheel" (19041905) has a detective effect. Writing about the Far East has "New Singapore Story" (1907), etc. At this time, there has been great progress in writing scenery. The reason why he wrote novels about England, America and Denmark is because the Gothic race is made up of England, America and Denmark. Jensen's writings are not only famous in Denmark, but also a representative in the Nordic literary world. Most of his novels have more than 100,000 words, and his novels similar to racial epics are the most famous. His six novels (1) "The Lost King" (1919), (2) "Ice Age" (the above two books are translated into English with the combined name "Fire and Ice"), (3) "Guest of the Goddess of Destiny" (1919), "Footsteps of the People of Zulberri" (1922), (5) "Ship" (1912), (6 "Columbus" (1921). His writing is as thoughtful and painstaking as Bazoc, and the time is very slow. The success of a masterpiece is not a matter of one or two years. This epic-like novel can be divided into four periods: (1) the Ice Age, (2) the Racial Migration Era, (3) the Pirate Era, (4) the Discovery of America Era. The Ice Age was during the Racial Migration Era. What he wrote was a myth. In ancient times, there were hail and rain in the sky, and the people on the earth were all killed. At this time, only one person was left. He desperately rushed north, and met a woman on the way. The man was extremely happy. Later, he fell in love with the woman. This is what happened in the first two books. Later, the man was not satisfied with the current environment, so he discovered his new plan and drifted to an island to live, and later gave birth to many descendants of the Danish people, until the era of the discovery of America. His six novels have the same ambition as Turgenev in terms of quantity. Since then, he has also written five "Myths" (1907-1924), Jorgine (1926), (and three collections of poems, "Poetry" (1906), "Four Seasons" (1923) and "Light of the World" (1926), essays include "The New World" (1907), "The Heart of the Northerner" (1912), "The Leader of Our Time" (1915) and other books,

Jakoh Kunhseh (I858-I9I7) is good at writing about local customs and the life of private school teachers in farmers' villages. He is also a soil writer in Denmark. Kunhseh has also expressed his own thoughts on philosophy and religion. He started writing articles very late, about forty years old. In his youth, he worked as a teacher in rural primary schools. The last twenty years of his life were devoted to lectures and writing. His "Philosophy of Life" shows his thoughts. He is also a religious revolutionary. He is dissatisfied with the religion at that time and has the main view of reform. In 1912, he wrote "Terror", and in 1914, he wrote "Courage", which is about the development of Lutheranism. His works are full of humor and ridicule. His works are mostly subjective, and he often uses the characters in the novel to promote his own thoughts. However, his thinking is against the new trend. Danish modern writers are probably the most zealous.

The Story of World Literature (1)(4)(7) by American John Macy, translated by Hu Zhongchi 182

Chapter 38: 19th Century French Prose

Maupassant relied on the economy of language and thought to create his effects. Émile Zola, the most prolific of the naturalists or realists, piled up minute details, relying entirely on weight to achieve his effect. Compared to him, even Balzac seemed concise and thrifty, while Maupassant was nothing more than bones. Zola's novels are grand in their collective power. All of life is gathered within them, to the point that the reader is almost satiated with life itself, wishing there were not so much of it. Zola lacked the finest French charm and elegance, and the French critical world dealt with him with sharp sarcasm. There are no masterpieces or gems in any of Zola's works. However, if we were to select two or three from his countless works, we could mention "Nana," "The Debacle," and "The Earth." These and many others have been translated into English because his strength lies in his content, not in the magic of a particular style. Continued on page 9.

Page 24

Page 25

Therefore, he loses almost nothing in translation. Zola's critics reproach him for placing too much emphasis on ugliness, strangeness, and obscenity (of which his novels are undeniable proof). However, his view of life is not unhealthy, but rather that of a doctor simply recording the symptoms of pain, or of a social reformer informing us of the world's errors and hoping for its improvement. His initial successful work, "L'Assommoir" (The Dram Shop), is a great sermon against alcohol. There is no doubt about the sincerity of Zola's aims. The nobility of his character was demonstrated by his courageous battle in the Dreyfus Affair, which made him a national hero after his death.

The person who gave the eulogy at Zola's tomb was Anatole France, a figure as different from Zola as two Frenchmen could be. France, Monsieur, used his country's name as his literary name (which was actually) his father's name, a shortened form of François. And no one can have a more transcendent right to this name. He is original, independent, indulging in reverie in the safety of eccentricity, yet his eccentric spirit encompasses the finest elements of French tradition. If we have his books, it seems we can learn from those books his country, his era, and the French language taking its most complete form. What aspect of life has he not touched with sharp, vigorous, and clear skepticism? "L'Île des Pingouins" (Penguin Island) is a satirical history of civilization; Jonathan Swift would have smiled at it, and Voltaire would have paid homage to someone superior to himself. The four novels collected and called "Contemporary History" are realistic, with a glimmer of light. "Le Crime de Sylvestre Bonnard" (The Crime of Sylvestre Bonnard) is a romance with tears and smiles. When he encounters great problems, he is as sincere and passionate as his friend Zola, and he carries the burden of erudition that intimidates mere scholars so lightly on his towering shoulders. His ideas are often revolutionary, and his style is pure and simple. He hates deceit and hypocrisy, but his hatred is gentle, ironic, and philosophical, never becoming agitated due to anger. His genius is critical and analytical, and his novels are cleverly used vehicles for conveying his thoughts and opinions.

The nineteenth century was one of the richest periods of French prose. Novels and criticism flourished in both quality and quantity. Even without outstanding giants, modern France would have a great prose literature. In a century crowded with talented figures, it is difficult to say who stands out, and perhaps there is no need to say. This difficulty is particularly confusing when it comes to novels, where subject matter is subservient to public taste and critical judgment fluctuates rapidly. Although this does not need to trouble us.

One genius who has increased in value with time is Henri Beyle, who, as he called himself, was Stendhal. His novels "Le Rouge et le Noir" (The Red and the Black) and "La Chartreuse de Parme" (The Charterhouse of Parma) are remarkable in their analysis of character. These were published in the first half of the same century, but until Stendhal's death, they did not make much of an impression on people. Balzac understood his value, and later French writers recognized his influence, praising his genius. Rémy de Gourmont, the most magnificent of modern critics, regarded him as a touchstone. If we do not like him, then we can say that we do not belong to the "happy few," the chosen ones who understand.

The author who wrote novels for the happy many was Prosper Mérimée. His Corsican story "Colomba" is a complete story with a stinging content, in the same style as Mérimée's other works, written in a classically clear, yet full of poetic colour, style. His "Carmen" has a double claim to immortality, why? Because it is the material for the most immortal of operas, Bizet's libretto.

Alphonse Daudet, who is aptly called the French Dickens, is like the English master in his sorrow and humor, and in his heartfelt sympathy for all kinds of people, especially those ill-treated by life. In this respect, as he closely resembles Dickens, he also closely resembles Victor Hugo. His first novel to make him famous, "Le Petit Chose" (The Little Thing), is full of generosity and gentleness, and is free from objectionable sentimentality, as is true of the subsequent books that made him ever more beloved by the public. The charm of his style (and of his entire human being, more or less) earned the respect of writers such as Zola, Flaubert, and the Goncourts, who held a much more critical and analytical view of life than he did. He belongs to the naturalist school, as well as to the school of mockers and humorists. His "Tartarin de Tarascon" is one of the finest literary farces.
